<Author>geordy
<Content>Very Happy Here! Made a decision to stay on the right bank last trip and this hotel seemed perfect. Good reviews, centralish location..okay the Movie background! It is a small , lovely hotel in a very old building. Our room was one of the largest I've had in Paris and it was just a standard double bed room with bath. Interesting furnishings and details.I always insist on A/C in Sept. but only needed it the first afternoon...and that was only because we were actually in the hotel in the afternoon because we were not able to check in until after one. The staff were all efficient, the elevator tiny but fortunarely working as we were on the 5th flooy(though we often walked down), did not take breakfast as there are plenty of cafes and such in the area.Very convenient if you are there for shopping, the Opera.... A little out of the way for first timers..I'd stay closer to the Seine if a Paris newbie, but Metro and taxi stand right around the corner, as well as 3 cafes that are open even on Sunday, cash machines, stores for wine, water, snacks...Had a view of the tippy top of Sacre Coeur and Paris rooftops! No complaints!And the price is right! I won't say too much more...don't want the rates to increase!And now I have to rent the Movie!

<Author>dklaw
<Content>Unique Older Hotel Hotel Langlois is a classic older and smaller hotel, with all of the uniqueness and charm that you might expect. The lobby looks like it came out of a movie set, and there is a wire-cage lift for moving luggage up and down. (The wide stairway is perfectly adequate for walking.) We had a spacious room and bathroom on the front side of the hotel. There is some traffic noise if you leave the windows open, but generally things seemed to quiet down after midnight, at least on the weeknights. The hotel is conveniently located next to the Trinite Metro station, and there is a good bakery nearby, as well as several cafes and bistros. However, if you are planning to visit the major tourist attractions (Eiffel Tower, des Invalides, Museums, etc.), you may want to look for a hotel on the other side of the river, as it can be a bit of a walk. The neighborhoods around the Langlois are a mix of apartments and night clubs (Moulin Rouge is not too far away), which is a plus if you are looking to experience the real Paris rather than the typical tourist sites.

<Author>Sidso
<Content>Great Hotel :) Me and my wife stayed here from 2 November to 5 November (3 nights), and had a great time in this hotel. The room was clean and spacious, and had a very big bathroom. There was a minibar in the room which was very convenient for us (we like to drink white wine sometimes ;)). The elevator is a bit small, but we already knew that before we came. We liked the elevator, but i may be a bit awkward for elderly or those with a lot of luggage. The staff are very friendly, but the night staff spoke poor english. We got to use their PC, so it all worked out in the end.Location : The hotel is 2 blocks away from the Pigalle district (Moulin Rouge ++), and very close to the Metro station. The downside is that you'll have to change Metro a few times if you want to go to/from the Orly Airport for example. In some Metro Stations in Paris, there is a lot of stairs, so beware if you have a lot of luggage. Better to take a taxi then perhaps.The hotel is also very close to the Gare Du Nord trainstation. All in all me and my wife had a great time in Paris and we have no problem recommending it to others.

<Content>We loved the Hotel Langlois  We booked this hotel based on many great reviews here on Tripadvisor. Wow---I miss those croissants.English is widely spoken. Whenever, I had slight problems withmy lack of French, I would just smile, and have fun. Stay at the Langlois, and have a great trip.

<Author>seegage
<Content>Good Location and Value Following research on TA, I booked Hotel Langlois for a two night stay. Away from Paris Central meant affordable prices both for hotel and local restaurants. Generous room size with seperate washroom, TV and Air-con. Wi-Fi if you need it, but I deliberately left my laptop at home. Room was at front and could be a bit noisy at night, noisy in the day too at the moment due to building work but that is a temporary situation. Metro stop barely 100 metres away and the Paris Metro system doesn't take long to get used to - even for two days our 鈧?6 Orange cards were well worth it. If you prefer walking, its not so far out to be impractical - we walked back from the Louvre at 1am with no problem, though it pays to have some idea where you are going...Don't expect superlative service or fancy hotel procedures - what you see it what you get and we were not disaapointed, with the exception of breakfast which is best taken at one of the caf茅s round the corner.

<Author>Whitechurch
<Content>Comfortable but possibly over-priced The Hotel Langlois is a charming, comfortable and clean hotel with helpful staff. The only major downsides were the price and the noise (but only during the working day) from the very extensive renovations being carried out next door.It is conveniently located very near Trinite Metro station and plenty of eateries for anything from a quick coffee  croissant in the morning to a full evening meal.The furniture was very solid and traditional -- as was the plumbing in the bathroom which was as large as many a hotel bedroom.The lift has period charm but saves walking up many flights of stairs. Our room overlooked a central courtyard so we were not exposed to any traffic noise.The price was noticeably higher than the equally-convenient hotel which has just been refurbished (also a 2-star) that we have previously used in Paris.

<Author>Meaculpal
<Content>Nice Location, Nice Hotel My partner and I stayed at the Hotel Langlois in June 2008 for one night. We had been on an organized tour, and we wanted to stay in a hotel that was both reasonably priced and centrally located. This hotel fit the bill. The hotel is located within a few feet of the Trinte Metro stop, and it is close to several nice cafes and restaurants. One of the nice things about its location is that it is only a ten minute walk to the Roissey Bus to CDG. I would like to thank the entire staff at the hotel for a pleasant stay. The room was a good size, and the prices for the minibar were extremely reasonable. The room was also extremely quiet.The only complaint we had was the extremely hard bed, but that was minor compared to our overall good experience. I would recommend this property to anyone looking for a good location with good value.

<Author>dartmouthgirl
<Content>Great location We booked into the Hotel Langlois for two nights in May. My husband and I travelled with our four and-a-half year-old daughter. The location was perfect: two minutes' walk from the Metro, 5 minutes from fabulous shopping. There are cafes on the corner. The hotel provided a cot for our daughter at no extra charge. The room was charming and spacious enough. There was a mini fridge and a TV. Our room was on the fifth floor. Noise was not a problem. There was an ancient lift from the ground level that was small but worked just fine. We did not eat breakfast at the hotel. It was about 12 euros per person, which was very high. Much cheaper -- and more fun -- to eat at one of the cafes nearby.

<Author>Lanson2
<Content>Lovely comfortable hotel The hotel lived up to the expectations we had from reading reviews on TripAdvisor. Our room (14) on the first floor was spacious, warm and comfortable. Our bed was wide and really comfortable. The metro is just 100 metres away on the corner. (Tip: Bus 24 from Gare St. Lazare goes all the way down the river Seine to Gare de lyon where you can have coffee in the fabulous Train Bleu). Cheaper than the tour bus! From the Gare du Nord, you can also take bus No. 42 or 43 or 26 to Trinite near the hotel.Breakfast was very good. You can boil your own egg! Mini croissants, pains au chocolat, raisin croissants, cheese, meat, fruit salad, yoghurt, rolls, butter, honey, jams, marmalade, tea or coffee, olives, real milk (not long-life) cereals, chilled water, freshly squeezed orange juice, etc. The only gripe is that there isn't a lot a room in the breakfast room.Staff are attentive and friendly. We will ask for a room at the back next time as our room was noisy. Maybe this was because there was a transport strike the three nights we were there and everyone drove into town!

<Author>IndyBee
<Content>Roomy choice for Paris My husband, teenage daughter and I stayed here for two nights. Our room and bathroom were nice sized, large by Parisian standards, and the bathroom was enormous and well appointed. Also, easy 15-20 minute walk or very quick cab ride from where the Roissy Bus drops you off. <Author>ChristinaW
<Content>Beauitiful and Charming Parisan HOtel I stayed here three nights and was very pleased overall with the hotel and the room. I had a double and the room was larger than many Parisian hotel rooms, especially at that price range. It had a very nice new flat-screen TV, and beautiful furnishings, with excellent bathroom. The entire hotel is lovely, and the owner and other staff are very pleasant and helpful. I don't eat breakfast in hotels, so can't comment on that. The location is very convenient being so close to a metro stop, and there are a couple cafes at the corner with decent drinks and food, as well as a bakery next door and a good chocolate shop at the corner. I know Paris pretty well, though, and have been in this area before, so none of that was a surprise to me.Overall, I was very pleased with the accommodations for a 2* hotel, and it is really much nice than that, I think (as it as AC and large, beautiful rooms). The only drawbacks to the hotel is that is was somewhat noisy and the mattress, as someone else noted, is definitely harder than average and a little uncomfortable for that reason. Other guests were noisy in slamming their doors, and I know you can't blame the hotel for that, exactly (someone else said the bathroom door slammed, not sure, if so, that could be helped). However, I had a room on the second floor overlooking the courtyard with the idea that would be quieter. I don't think it was as there were some people down there who talked in very loud voices, a lot, and the noise echoes in those type of spaces. I don't know who they were -- if it was the building next door or the hotel's own staff, down there. The street isn't a main one, so I don't think the traffic would be much at night anyway, and the metro noise might have been a little better on a higher floor. As someone else noted, this hotel is apparently right on top of the metro lines, so you can hear the trains rumble when they run. At least they don't run from about 1 am until 5 am, but still, that was a little disturbing. It didn't make sleeping impossible, and I would stay there again, but I definitely heard them and it bothered me somewhat.  
<Date>Aug 13, 2007

<Author>EJaneWench
<Content>Good for kids My husband and I stayed in a suite (#44, I think) with our 3 children from June 12 through June 15. The hotel was clean and comfortable and the staff friendly. The kids (ages 7, 8 and 13) loved the elevator. We opted out of the hotel breakfast (only because our children do not eat 8 euros worth), but there is a wonderful bakery next door for breakfast pastries which we ate in the suite with coffee ordered up from the hotel (at a very reasonable price).The only downside is that the location is not the most convenient for the major tourist attractions. The Musee D'Orsay is only 3 or 4 Metro stops away, and from there we could take the BatoBus around to the sights on the Seine during the day, but returning back to the hotel from the Eiffel Tower at night (after 9 when the BatoBus shuts down) was difficult by Metro, requiring 2 transfers, so we convinced a taxi driver to let the 5 of us squeeze into his cab.Overall, a great experience.

<Author>Tennisnut4
<Content>The lovely Langlois Stayed here 3 nights in early June. Picked it because it was in The Guardian or The Observer paper review of top 20 hotels in Paris for under 拢100. It lived up to its selection. We noted French people were staying here as well as tourists.Hotel is on a quiet street; we had a rear room so no street noise. However, the hotel is situated above the metro lines so trains can be heard rumbling by underneath. This didn't bother us in sleeping as it is a far away rumble. The hotel has 24 rooms; all the stairways and floors are carpeted so again no footfall noise. Good standard of decoration, think red carpets and plush curtains with quirky light fittings. Comfy beds, good size rooms, very very friendly staff. Breakfast 11 euros - freshly squeezed orange juice is included or go to the patisserie along the street. We had the breakfast. Good location by Trinitie metro and its in the vicinity of the department stores.

<Author>Irishmoss
<Content>Lovely Hotel My husband and I just returned from a 6 night stay at the Hotel Langlois. We enjoyed a quiet, spacious room with a small but very nice bath with tub for a very reasonable 130 Euros per night. Everything was clean, the staff was nice, and breakfasts were quite good and reasonably priced (for Paris at least) with enough food to hold us over until dinner. While there are no non-smoking rooms, our room was fresh and there was no residual smell - but we could smell smoke from other rooms, we assume through the venting system, which was a bit unpleasant on occasion. The big and heavy doors in the hotel were easy to accidently slam and the bathroom doors made slamming noises if you closed them tight, but our sleep was not disturbed by this. What did keep us awake was that the beds here are HARD, much more so than we are accustomed to at home and much more so than other places we have stayed (three others on this trip alone). While this hotel had pillows available in the closet (many European hotels do not) they were well-used and had obviously been around for quite a while. Location-wise, there are much prettier areas of Paris to stay in and they are better located to the things my husband and I enjoy when we are visiting. We also came across some street people bedding down for the night at the Trinity Church nearby but they certainly weren't threatening to us or anything - it was just a bit of a surprise and I would probably avoid this area later in the evening. The Opera House is near by but when we've attended opera performances in Paris, they've always been at the new facility quite a distance from here. Two of the major department stores are a few minutes away and they are fun to check out for a short while, but they are not the reason most of us go to this beautiful city. Although it's true that the Metro is right around the corner, I personally prefer to walk to our favorite sights as much as possible and this location didn't allow for that. That said, we found a couple of really nice restaurants in the area by using the Pudlo Guide (found at Rick Steve's favorite English language book store, the Red Wagon - well worth the visit.) and I managed to drop more than a few Euro in some of the antique shops nearby. While it's not perfect (what is?) we would certainly recommend Hotel Langlois as a lovely hotel in Paris.

<Author>Gaelic999
<Content>Superb Hotel We both stayed at the hotel im May for a special Birthday. The location of the hotel is ideal for exploring Paris. You are about 10 minutes walk from the Opera and all the sights beyond that.Hotel: The hotel is old world paris with its fireplaces and antiques in the bedrooms. The lift is amazing with it's iron frame and heavy wood interior. The hotel is on a very quiet street, but really has no views of the Parisian skyline. The staff speak some English, and are willing to help and offer guidance when prompted. We had breakfast in the hotel one morning which was very good.Locality: The hotel is right on the trinity Metro line which provides access to the whole of Paris. We purchased the 10 ticket deal which was ideal for our 3 day stay (tickets are so so cheap!!) .There are plenty of little restaurants close by the hotel with decent food. We went to the 6th floor restaurant for breakfast at La Fayette which was excellent and had superb views of Paris.Sights: We bought a two day open top bus pass, which was superb...1st time we have done this in a city. Some of the sights look close, but are a bit of a distance on foot. The bus is ideal as you can get on and off as often as you like over the two days. You can also add in a riverboat cruise to the ticket. We didn't fid it at all expensive, but ran out of time for the boat cruise. Tickets are valid for two years so we will be back!Dining: There is no smoking ban in Paris, so coming from Scotland we found the smoking in restaurants very unpleasant. I would say do your research on restaurants and try to book in advance, don't rely on finding somewhere nice for that evening as you will probable end up in a tourist restaurant. Watch out many of the cafe's and restaurants all offer the same menu.We had two meals one excellent and the other the best meal ever.We dined in the Juiles Verne restaurant on the second floor of the Eiffel Tour. We couldn't fault it and the meal was first class. It was such a romantic venue and the view over Paris was amazing. It was very expensive - so ideal for special occasions.Overall the hotel made a very comfortable, ideally located base to explore Paris. We would most certainly use this hotel the next time we are in Paris.

<Author>TravellerMO
<Content>Great little hotel that grows on you After reading many uniformly good reviews on TripAdvisor, we decided to stay at the Hotel Langlois on our holiday in Paris in March 2007. Located on a narrow street close to the Opera, the frontage of the hotel onto the street is so small one could easily walk past it and not notice. When we (wife, daughter and self), first saw the hotel, we were a bit taken aback. We have, over the years been used to staying in big, modern hotels in various countries, so this came as a bit of a surprise. The hotel is very old and has a storied history, so do not be surprised if you are initially disappointed - as we were - by the small and seemingly shabby reception area. The lift, off to one side of this small lobby, is very small too 鈥?sort of an an iron cage that creaks its way up and down slowly!! This too, is clearly a vintage contraption.We were greeted at the reception by a very friendly young lady who quickly checked us in. We were given a suite, facing the street. As I mentioned, the hotel is old and has the same old style architecture and layout till today, so when we walked in to our suite 鈥?such as it was 鈥?we felt let down. The room was old, as was the furniture. We continued to feel disappointed. But as we spent some more time in the room we realized that contrary to initial appearance, it was very clean. The bedlinen was clean and the bathroom was fairly large and very clean. The towels were fresh and white. The room heater worked very well The maids came in daily to clean the rooms, change linen etc. The limited breakfast served in the dining room on the ground floor was also quite good. The best part of the hotel is the location. The Paris underground is fabulous and there is a station just a couple of minutes down the street from the hotel. Since it is in the Opera district, it is pretty centrally located and close to many attractions. The Hop 鈥?On, Hop 鈥?Off Paris bus tour stop is about a ten minute walk away and there are any number of very good restaurants and cafes within a five to ten minute walk in any direction from the hotel. The staff at the reception were always friendly and helpful and ever ready to offer us advice on 鈥渢ouristy鈥?activities in Paris. I can confidently say that we did not have a single bad experience with the hotel during our stay 鈥?absolutely nothing to complain about at all. So if you are looking for a great little hotel centrally located in Paris, this could well be it. Charming, cozy and friendly, Langlois is a hotel that grows on you.

<Author>eatigs
<Content>Excellent value at this friendly, quaint hotel Our family (young couple and one-year-old child) stayed at the Hotel Langlois for four nights, Feb.25-28, 2007. We very much enjoyed our stay and would happily recommend the hotel to all value-conscious travellers. (We'd give it a rating of 4.5 if we could...) The hotel, a renovated bank from the 1800s, has considerable character and both the reception and cleaning staff are warm and accomodating (although some have limited English). Our room (#55) was very spacious and pleasantly, if simply decorated. The baby cot we had requested was set up while we were checking in, so that it was ready when we moved in. If we leaned out the bathroom window, we could see the Trinity church nearby - about the best view possible, given the hotel's location on a narrow side street. The antique (original?) elevator is a real adventure: it is attractively oak-panneled with an open swinging door but is extremely small and lurches frighteningly when it stops, often at the wrong floor. We found it great fun, but it is clearly the bane of the staff's existence and would be very unsuitable for those who are nervous, claustrophobic or mobility-impaired. As far as advantages, the hotel's location is good, quiet and yet very close to a metro station. The free internet access in the breakfast room is a real plus (although the wireless access is unreliable). We did not eat at the hotel, but the breakfast buffet looked nice and twice the staff thoughtfully gave our baby a fresh croissant when we left in the morning. I liked their key system: each time you leave, you drop your pass key off at reception and the 24-hour desk attendant welcomes you and returns it when you arrive back - no lost keys and the cleaning staff knows when your room is empty. The mini-bar prices were better than most of those in the local shops, so we drank very many bottled waters and juices and then were only charged for a few. They also found us an adapter to allow us to charge our cell phone. For 130 euro a night, we found this hotel to be a great value. The highlight for us was the pleasant, family atmosphere - the staff were unfailingly friendly and eager to help.

<Author>Steve2006Dublin
<Content>3rd Time Staying Here! My wife, my three children and myself have stayed at Hotel langlois now on three occasions in the past three years. This time we had a suite on the 4th Floor - 42. This hotel cannot be beaten for value for money, ambience and location. We have always found the staff very friendly and professional without being intrusive. The breakfast has gone up to 鈧?1 each, but, is still great value and useful when with kids. This time our youngest (8 years old) could walk everywhere! The Louvre, Musee D'Orsay, even the Eiffel Tower and Left Bank were all manageable. As regards shopping, well, the main shops (Printemps, Galleries Lafayette, GAP) are literally two blocks away. We also got out without the kids to the very atmospheric Bistro des Deux Theatres, just around the corner at the side of Trinite Church. 3 Course meal with coffees PLUS a choice of a bottle of wine at 鈧?4 each was great value. The Trinite Metro stop is 200m away. There is a superb pattisserie on the same street for stashing up with lunchtime rolls and pastries. Some good Italian restaurants also nearby. One suggestion, if travelling from CDG Airport. Take the train to Gare De Nord and the metro from Magenta (next to Gare De Nord) to Gare St Lazare, from where you can take the 10min walk to the hotel.

<Author>Heelntoe
<Content>Loved the Langlois We booked the Langlois after reading many positive reviews in Trip Advisor, and were not disappointed. We were given room 31, which we were quite happy with, especially with the artwork and the ceramic cat on the fireplace. The bathroom was the size of a small bedroom! Our stay did not include breakfast, so we walked down a few stores to the left to the Artisan Boulangerie and had an almond croisant for breakfast, which was a meal in itself. Many of our wonderful lunches came from that Boulangerie, but we were disappointed to find them closed on the weekend. We had 2 good, reasonably priced meals at Chartier, a 5 minute walk from the hotel, and 2 wonderful meals at Bistro de deux theatres at 18 rue Blanche, a 2 minute walk. All the hotel personnel were nice, especially since we tried to speak French as much as we felt comfortable doing. The Trinite metro station at the end of the block was a quick way to start our local travel. But walking around is the best way to get a feel for the charm of Paris. When we return, we definitely will choose the Hotel Langlois as our base.

<Content>Good for kids We thought this hotel was well located and good value for money. Our triple room was very spacious with an enormous bathroom. Unfortunately we overlooked a very dismal void between buildings, but i'm sure the rooms facing the road are better. Our teenagers had a very pleasant room on the ground floor beside reception looking out onto a pretty courtyard (at the bottom of the dismal void) The ancient lift was a novelty, and some of the bumps and lurches were as good as the Disney rides (I notice another review where the lift is not working!) With regard to the location which as your other reviews have pointed out is excellent for transport and shopping, i should also mention that at the end of the street in front of the Eglise de la Trinite there is a childrens playground, where i spent some time everday with my 7 year old letting off steam after sightseeing. It was fun watching the nannies and their immaculately dressed charges. The playground had an outdoor tabletennis table, and i asked at reception if they had any bats and a ball, which they didn't (wouldn't cost much!) The staff were helpful and my only criticism would be breakfast, which is uncomfortably cramped, and guests have to squeeze past each other to get to the buffet table.

<Author>tangerine74
<Content>If you want a Paris hotel that feels Parisian... I booked a double room at the hotel Langlois after reading positive reviews on Trip Advisor, and on the whole, was pretty pleased with what we got. Our room (31) was big, with a large bathroom, and while the decor erred on the vintage side of chic, the old furnishings gave the place a great deal of character, often missing from anonymous city hotels. Big double bed (but small pillows), lots of hot water, TV, wardrobe - and we didn't have a problem with noise from other rooms at all. And as other reviews have mentioned, the old-fashioned lift and the helpful French staff make it a characteristically Parisian experience.Location is very good, about 2 minutes' walk from Trinite metro station, and the Metro itself is as easy to navigate as the London underground. Montmartre is just a few stops north, and it takes no time to get to the major central attractions. We skipped breakfast in the hotel in favour of nearby cafes or boulangeries, of which there are plenty. Downsides? Make sure you bring your own toiletries, or buy some from the Monoprix nearby: the soaps and shampoo sachets are really horrible, stingy offerings, and there's not even a facecloth. Our room was freshly cleaned when we arrived, but it did smell very pungently of fragranced cleaning products, to the point where we had to leave the windows open during the day, just to air the place - if you're a non-smoker with sensitive nose, ask for a non-smoking room!

<Author>Simone39
<Content>A real piece of Paris! My husband and I stayed at this hotel from 1-4 December. We go to Paris quite a lot and I really liked the look of this hotel. We were given room 15, on the first floor. If you look at the picture of the hotel, ours was the two left hand windows. The bedroom was huge, with no less than six lamps to create a lovely warm and cosy atmosphere, marble fireplace, oil paintings and art deco furniture. There was a table and two chairs which was a useful touch.The bathroom was amazing - lovely and big, unusual in Paris, again with a marble fireplace, a lamp and huge mirror. Usually we hop in and out of the shower in a bathroom that is on the compact side to say the least, so it was rather nice after a long day pounding the streets of Paris to soak in a hot bath pondering on the hotel's history (it used to be a bank).We skipped the breakfast, which looked very good, in favour of mingling with Parisians at little cafes, or enjoying the panoramic view from the cafe at the top of Galeries Lafayette (another reviewer's recommendation).There were a couple of minor downsides - the toiletries weren't up to much, just sachets of shampoo which we had to double up as bath foam, and being at the front there was a lot of street noise. Mainly traffic (and the rumble of the metro, which I quite liked bizarrely) but also loud noises coming from the renovations of a building up the road. But I don't mind noise so if you do, ask for a room at the back. You can also hear the bells of the Trinity Church which I definitely liked!The young girl at the desk was quite friendly, and after a day in Paris and being a bit damp from the rain, she was more than happy to bring us hot chocolate and coffee to the room, beautfiully presented on a lace-lined silver tray.I would definitely go back here again, I used to think hotel rooms were just somewhere to lay your head whilst you got on with making the most of Paris, but I felt at home and that added an extra something to our stay.

We loved the hotel as it has character and you really feel you are living like a Parisian. The room and bathroom were very clean and the towels are fluffy. Despite the cold weather the hotel was cosy and warm. The hotel is so near the metro that you can travel anywhere in the city very quickly. Of course, it's proximity to Galeries Lafayette and the shopping area didn't influence our choice of hotel at all.

<Author>gmc2508
<Content>Charming hotel and a great 2* choice I booked the Hotel Langlois following the favourable reviews from Trip Advisor and I was not disappointed. For a 2 star hotel, the service and room were very pleasant indeed. On checking in, I was given the key to room 23 and took the elevator to the 2nd floor with a heavy case. (Tip - remember to close the interior elevator door on entering and leaving!). The room was a double, facing towards the Rue Sainte-Lazare. The bed was very large and two square pillows were provided, as well as a long bolster-style pillow (which I didn't find terribly comfortable but perhaps others will!).The room comprised a double mirrored-wardrobe, television, small refridgerator, three wicker chairs, a guest table, two bedside tables. In one corner was a marble fire-surround/radiator grill upon which sat a marble bust in front of a large mirror. The room was also air-conditioned (optional, and controllable in the room), and had a small balcony/French windows looking into the street. The bathroom was compact and not terribly well-lit, but had a hair-dryer, shower/bath, toilet, sink and shaver point next to a mirror. The housekeeping at the hotel was not intrusive but the rooms were well-maintained. The staff at the reception desk were helpful and friendly throughout my stay from the 18th-24th October. I did not take breakfast in the hotel as several other options were available nearby, including a patisserie on the same street. The location of the hotel was good for sightseeing, given the proximity to the Metro line 12 station Trinite and also the Gare St Lazare for other lines, including that to Versailles. My one (very small) negative comment is that although the hotel has one computer terminal with internet access in the breakfast room, I would have appreciated free wifi in the rooms, and would have probably paid a little more for the room, was the service available.I would recommend the Hotel Langlois for those sightseeing in Paris and the standard of the rooms for a 2-star hotel exceeded my expectations. I would return to the hotel for another stay, especially if wifi access could be provided!

<Author>john4rmdublin
<Content>Quaint, oozed charm, central to shopping, unassuming...just loved it ! Have visited Paris numerous times and only this once feel required to tell all and sundry about the wonderfull experience we had in the Hotel Langlois. Had the pleasure of staying here over the paddys day weekend in 2005 . Just loved all to do with it ! The hotel is small, quirky, quiant, quintessential parisian charm without the pomp. The staff were professional, pleasant, unobtrusive. Our room was on the 6th floor with a slightly obscured view of Sacre Cour over the rooftops. Bathroom was small but spotlessly clean with a half bath. The room was simply furnished in a 'shabby chic' style that was sympathethic to the era of the hotel. This may not be to everyone's tastes but we found it utterly engaging and charming. The matress was firm and afforded us an excellent nights sleep.The hotel can be a tad difficult to find, it being on a one way street that need to be approached from the opposing end if travelling by taxi. Nonetheless, it is centrally located, the main shopping streets being a max 10 mins stroll away. Breakfast was simple, tasty and continental, served in a small bright ante room. In the mornings, we woke up to the the aromas of the patisseries along the block that wafted up to our room.....wonderful....!!! Esentially we loved the hotel...the only slight problem was that there is an overflow family room on the very top floor above our room. Just the one night, this was occupied by a large young family that had to catch an early flight....let us say, that the sound of young children being woken in the middle of the night and their attendant tantrums did carry through the wood floor to our room. However, we were so pleased with the hotel that something like this, which was beyond the hotel's control, will not dent or enthusiasm for this place. It is not the George V, and does not pretend to be but we loved it's simplicity quaint charm !!!.....a little gem !

<Author>pvmkmyer
<Content>Loved the Hotel Langlois My wife and I stayed at the Hotel Langlois for 6 nights in February around Valentine's Day, based upon recommendations on Tripadvisor. It lived up to all our expectations.My wife is handicapped. They assigned us a large room with an enormous bath on the 1st floor. Unfortunately, after we got up to the room the romantic, but aged, elevator broke. They relocated us to a ground floor room which we enjoyed very much for the remained of our stay. It took a couple days for the part to arrive for the elevator, so it's a good thing we opted for the ground floor room. The hotel is spotlessly clean and the bathroom had all the modern touches, including a hairdryer. Breakfast was added on to the bill and was very good. In addition to the normal French breakfast of one baguette and one croissant, they had a spread of cheeses and cold meats; yogurts; an egg cooker, fruit, and a variety of regular and sweet breads and rolls, including croissants. Although breakfast would have been cheaper at the cafe down the street, we felt it was (1) worth the money; and (2) worth the convenience since it was February and we didn't want to venture out in the cold and drizzle just to save a couple euros.We met our friends from Belgium at the hotel. She is a travel agent and was impressed with the hotel. She thought that the only reason it was government rated as 2* instead of 3* was because the breakfast room is small. Apparently a 3* is supposed to be able to seat a larger percentage of its guests at one time. it is definitely nicer than other 3* hotels I've stayed in.The staff was helpful; the breakfast waitress was very friendly albeit with very limited English. The location is convenient. Because of my wife's handicap we cannot take the Metro, but there was a taxi stand at the end of the street in front of the Trinite church. BTW, there is a wonderful unknown chocolate shop just to the right of the church as you are facing it from the front. We will be returning to the Hotel Langlois hopefully this December and looking forward to our stay.

<Author>zolo
<Content>The Longer I Stayed Here, The More I Liked It My review will read negative. I did enjoy staying here, but wanted to counterbalance some of the overly-effusive 5 star reviews. I got off on the wrong foot with the property mostly over problems that were not the Hotel Langlois' fault. First, I had severe jet lag coupled with having landed in what I consider a confusing city. Second, I booked the room over a year ago when it had percolated to #2 on the tripadvisor rating scale (!) and hence was due to be disappointed. You need to remember that this is still an old style, two star hotel with all that that entails, i.e. street noise, paper-thin walls so that you can hear conversations next door, some rooms with tiny bathrooms, small closet space with not enough hangers, no ironing board, no coffee maker, no clock of any kind and finally a pleasant enough concierge whose job discription is less travel agent/confident (as you find in an expensive hotel) and more security guard/busybody. We were celebrating our 25th and were quoted 120 euros ($180 in my currency), not what I call 'budget'. The first room shown to us had a huge bathroom, and a view of...a wall. I asked to see another room and to her credit, the concierge showed me #63; tastefully decorated, tiny bathroom (but with tub, so usefull after walking all day!) and the killer view looking north at the Sacre Couer. We took it with no regrets. Moral; ask to see more than one room if possible. Getting back to the function of the concierge, when I asked for directions to a tourist bureau, she looked at me as if she had never been requested this before. Right then I knew I was on my own with regards to finding out what's on in town, making dinner reservations and deciphering the mass transit. When asking for multiple room keys, she explained the custom of only giving out one and when you leave, handing it to the person at the desk. I guess it's for security, but it can still get awkward when you both go off on seperate itineries. Anyway, I did get over the jet lag, calmed down and started to get in the vacation groove. And yes, I must agree that it is a very quaint hotel in a marvellous city. I loved the old, tiny elevator (reminded me of an old favourite in San Fran), just remember to close the inner door! The neighbourhood was nice as well, not touristy, but convenient to the sites and safe. You can feel like a Parissienne staying here. Below, dear reader, is some description of the locale to hopefully help you get acclimatized fast.As you step out of the hotel and head left towards the square you will run into a charmingly staffed patisserie. Patisseries in general (and this one is no exception) are the best deals in Paris. You can get a baguette, a delicious pastry and a 250 ml bottle of wine for less than 5 euros. One of our best remembrances was bringing said groceries back to the room, and snacking in front of the open window. Remember to bring/buy some wine glasses. Next to the patisserie is a nice cafe. Cafes are the worst deal in Paris. If you need a coffee, consider drinking at the bar like many commuters, you will be charged half the price. Also, they do not seem to have coffee-to-go in Paris and it is the next strongest thing to expresso. If you find it too strong, consider a cafe-au-lait. Next to the cafe is the Trinite metro located on the very convenient North-South #12 line. The metro is great, but can be daunting to a first-timer. This station has a manned booth but no photo-booth which you may need if you are considering the Carte d'Orange. I brought an extra passport photo which worked in the end. Walking is great in Paris but the metro is convenient and if I had to do it over again, would have taken the bus more. I would have killed for a map with the bus and subway lines justaposed over the streets, although I realise it would have been awfully busy. As you look out at the square, to your left is the way to Galleries Lafayette which is right next to the Opera which is where the RoissyBus drops you off. This is an economical and easy way to get to the hotel is you don't mind schlepping your bags four blocks. The map on the hotel website will make it easy for you to find it. Getting back to the square, if you go right instead for a short block, you will hit the Bistro des Deux Theatres, a prix-fixe only bistro where you get a kir, appetizer, entree, bottle of wine (limited selection), dessert and coffee for 33 euros. We found the experience fantastic. Finally, out of the hotel, if you head right instead of left and head up the road that veers north you will soon find the tiny Musee Gustave Moreau. If you are interested in the Museum pass, it's easiest just to buy it here, the clock does not start ticking until your first real visit. You will be hard pressed to break even on the pass, but it also can save you a lot of time in line. It gets you almost everywhere with the Eiffel Tower being the most notable exception. Also, even though my guide books were dated 2006, they wrote about 1,3 and 5 day passes when, in fact, they have moved on to 2,4 and 6. I hope these tips help you and just remember that the stereotype of the snootty French is most undeserved. Always say bonjour and try to speak there language no matter how broken your French is and they will meet you halfway and show you the secrets to their beautiful city. Bon voyage!  
<Date>Oct 4, 2006

<Author>Podger
<Content>Real Paris - My sister  I stayed here in May of this year. Of all the Parisian hotels I've stayed in over the years this has to be one of the best experiences. Near to just about everywhere you want to visit, close to buses and Metro, this hotel is in a less touristy part of Paris  in a more authentic area where local Parisians, work, shop and eat. Galleries Lafayette  Au Printemps are just down the street, the Opera House behind them. Monmartre is a short walk away along winding streets and then a short hike or 'Funicular up to the Sacre Coeur area. The hotel was clean, quiet and friendly - plumbing excellent and breakfasts good.We had a room on the 4th floor overlooking the street which was very bright  we were not distubed by noise from traffic or other hotel guests. We took a taxi from Gare du Nord to the hotel but the metro is very easy  the station about 1 minute away. I'll stay here next time I visit Paris for sure.

<Author>rabatabar
<Content>Charming and Good Value Would recommend this hotel to friends and will return. Exceptionally clean and friendly place. Interesting decor, furniture and comfortable surroundings. Charming as opposed to corporate. 120 euros for a very large room. Friends paid 89 euros for smaller doubles. All happy with rooms. TV with CNN, BBC and fridge. Top floor observation deck also gives a good and free vantage point of Opera and beyond. Plenty of cafes around hotel, but best meal of weekend was at Willis Wine Bar on Petit Champs 20 minutes walk away. 34 euros for 3 courses.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Best Value for the Money We are so glad we stayed at the Hotel Langlois in July 2006. We were there for three nights and the hotel was the best value for the money of any place we stayed on our two-week France vacation. We paid 120 Euros per night. The staff was very polite, friendly, helpful, and English-speaking. Hotel Langlois is extremely clean. The air conditioning worked perfectly. The hotel is in a great location. The metro is just a block away and the RER is about three blocks away. The easiest way to get from the airport to the hotel is to take the RER since you have the advantage of escalators and fewer changes when dealing with luggage. There is a computer in the breakfast area that you can use after 11am for free. It was very convenient. Breakfast is also served at the hotel for an additional price. However, there are also a variety of other places you can go to within walking distance. There was a refrigerator and TV in our room which were both very nice. Although the hotel claims their windows are soundproof, you can still hear a little bit of outside noise. However, since the hotel is located on a fairly quiet street the noise was not an issue. Printemps, a large department store is located nearby. We thoroughly enjoyed our stay and would definitely stay here again. We wholeheartedly recommend this hotel to other travelers.  
<Date>Jul 16, 2006

<Author>MOnica9
<Content>Good, but some issues We chose this hotel based on a great review in a newspaper for our trip to Paris. My mother, father and myself booked a double room with an extra bed. The extra bed was very hard and not very comfortable. I woke up several times each night with pain in my back. Didn't feel very well rested in the mornings. My parents lied in the double bed and had no complaints about the bed. Another irritating thing was the housekeeper. One morning she came into our room without knocking. And although we were 3 people we only got two big towels. One morning I took one towel (for the next morning) from the trolley and put it in the room before we went out. When we got back in the evening she had been in the room and removed it. Very annoying to say the least. I had to use the small towel intended for use after hand- washing every morning. And why was she in our room when the room was already done?The people in the reception was just ok, not too friendly and they rarely even looked up from the computer when we passed the desk. Breakfast was ok, it cost 10 euros per person, the food was high quality and tasty. The aircondition worked fine (thank god, it was over 30 degrees fahrenheit every day)All in all a good experience and I would stay there again, but a little bit more friendliness from the staff and more discretion from the housekeepers would be nice.

<Author>Middle-Age-Traveller
<Content>Just what we expected! I booked this hotel after reading your reviews. Was a bit nervous as I was arranging the trip for myself and a French friend who might be critical but we were both delighted. The hotel is near to the Metro and to RER station Haussman-Lazare from Gare du Nord Magenta. We had large quiet room number 11 on first floor at rear of hotel, no view but lovely large bathroom with lots of character. Rooms spotless and towels changed every day. Dining room is small but pretty and lots to eat but you can have breakfast in your room at no extra cost, this is customary in Paris hotels apparently. The staff were friendly, my friend's French no doubt helped, she said that few of the staff were actually French although I couldn't tell from the accent.We had a super meal at les Deux Theatres restaurant, set menu with lots of choices for33 Euros inclusive of a bottle of wine between two and coffee plus a sparkling wine aperitif.The hotel is handy for the sights with a combination of metro and walking. We found that a Paris Museum Pass was handy to skip the queues at Musee d'Orsay and Louvre but didn't save money unless you are a museumaholic. Would definitely return to this hotel.

<Author>pathni
<Content>Beautiful Break!!! I read the reviews on Tripadvisor and decided to book a three night break at the hotel Langlois, Paris. When we arrived we were warmly welcomed and were pleasantly surprised by the size and decor of our rooms. Lovely high ceilings and a real ambience that can only be experienced when in Paris! The hotel reception were always very helpful and friendly, and ensured that our stay was a memorable one. We asked about reservations for the Moulin Rouge show and the reception immediately contacted them and reserved our table...which ended up being one of the best spots in the theatre! As for location the Hotel Langlois is close proximity to everything, a 15 minute walk to Montematre, same again to the Champs Elysee, close to the large shopping centres, and with a metro within literally 50 meters nothing in Paris is more than a few minutes away. There are a number of relatively inexpensive cafe/ bistros close by and a delicious pattisserie at the corner. All in all I would highly recommend for anyone to stay at the Hotel Langlois, in fact I have booked my second stay for August this year!!!

<Author>ga2607
<Content>Good value in a nice area I picked the Hotel Langlois because of its high ratings on Trip Advisor and positive reviews in various guidebooks. I was not disappointed. Staff were very friendly and helpful, going out of their way to make us feel welcomed. We had reserved a standard double, but upon arrival we were told the room was not available the first night, so we would be put in a smaller room at a reduced rate and given a free breakfast. The room was small but was okay. Breakfast was fresh and offered a good selection. The next night they moved all our stuff to a very large room that we occupied the rest of our stay. Area around the hotel is not touristy, but is very convenient to the metro for getting to tourist destinations, especially the Montmartre-Pigalle area. Plenty of interesting places to eat all around the hotel. We and our friends were the only Americans at the hotel during our stay. If you need to stay at a Holiday Inn or Hilton or must have everyone around you able to speak english, this isn't the place for you. But if you want to stay someplace that has its own character and want to get the true feel and flavor of Paris, then this may be the right place at a very reasonable price.

<Author>Spirit
<Content>A Good Value and We Were Happy Here We stayed here in early May, 2006. Considering the price of hotels in Paris, this hotel is quite a bargain.The staff are nice.Three of us stayed in a two room suite. We had a big bed and two sort of cot sized fold out beds. I didn't sleep on the fold out beds but apparently they were adequate. The rooms were quite spacious, they were clean, and service was good.The elevator is a relic of a long bygone era It's small and quaint, and in very good condition!. There are a pair of doors behind the front door of the elevator. These inner doors have to be closed for the elevator to work. Hotel guests keep forgetting to close those doors, or don't know they have to, and then the elevator won't move. The young man at the desk is frequently running up the stairs to get the elevator. (He is in very good shape!)We went to the corner caf茅 for coffee and croissants every morning, but the breakfast room in the hotel looked nice鈥tarchy white tablecloths, coffee, big glasses of orange juice鈥 don鈥檛 know what else they had, but people in there looked happy!I had wondered if we would like the location of the hotel since it is in the 9th arrondissement. It turned out that I did like it. Most tourists stay in the arrondissements surrounding the Seine: 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, and 7. Those areas are maximally thick with tourists. After spending a day in the Saint Germain area I felt like I needed elbow room and was very happy to go back to the 9th which is mostly French. The Saint Lazare Metro station is at the corner of the hotel鈥檚 block. It could hardly be more convenient. A taxi stand is also at that corner. There鈥檚 a computer with Internet in the breakfast room which is available for use without charge. One of my friends made daily calls to Florida from our room and the charges for the calls were not high. We heard very little noise from the street in our rooms. All three of us were quite satisfied with this hotel.

<Author>jimjade3
<Content>We are Langlois fans I selected this hotel due to an interest in having my wife and daughter get a sense of an old Parisian experience without breaking the bank. I was attracted to the open cage elevator and the photos on Tripadvisor. My wife is a bit particular and her friends warned against 2 star hotels in Paris, so I was a little concerned. It turned out to be a great value and very good experience for all of us. The location is not in the midst of Paris tourism (a plus for us) but the metro is a half block away and it's a short and easy ride almost anywhere. It is on a little narrow side street with a good patisserie and a few other little cafes. My daughter's favorite Paris chocolate shop is around the corner. The lobby is small but cheerful with the little original caged elevator encircled by curving stairs. I had tried to reserve a suite as there were three of us but they said all suites were booked. It was a shock when we entered our room (about 4 per floor) through oversized double doors to find a large living room (with extra bed formed by folding out a chair) connected to a comfortable bedroom by oversized double doors, and a large renovated bath as well. There were all sorts of touches which showed thoughtful and low-key design of the type which might have been found 100 or so years ago. Marble busts, paintings, brass and mirrored coat rack, ....However, the phones, water pressure, TV's and other modern conveniences worked well and it was very clean. On the downside, the staff members are not particularly personable. They wake you up on time without fail and give you some basic answers but little else. Do not go there is you require concierge service as there is none of that. The fare for 4 nights was about 450 euros which made it an excellent value. As some reviewers have made mention, there is some noise. A few footsteps overhead, a laugh in the corridor, cycles reverberating against close buildings, a radiator clank. But to be honest we walked so far and were so beat that we slept very well. The management has invested in systems to improve sound. The large double casement windows appear old but tney have been replaced and they are further protected by new exterior pull down awnings and very thick interior drapes, as is the entrance double door. They could have gutted the place and produced soundproof generic boxes...but thankfully the owners have chosen to let you remember that you are in Paris.

<Content>Disappointed Booked my 3 night stay here because of all the great reviews, even though it was a bit above my budget. I might pluck up the courage to stay here again, as everyone else seems to have had fun, but I would request a room facing off the street and higher up - avoid the front rooms on the first floor!!!

<Author>Flitcraft
<Content>Great little hotel My daughter and I spent a week at the Hotel Langlois and highly recommend it. We had originally planned on not taking the optional breakfast, but ended up doing it almost every day for convenience and to fill us up for the day. In addition to the usual French pastry and bread they had sliced cold meat, eggs to boil, sliced cheeses, and Turkish cheese and oil cured olives. Also orange juice and tea if wanted plus plenty of good French cafe. Very convenient location--only a half block from the Trinite metro station, and about four blocks from the Opera Garnier (where the Roissybus from the airport stops). Also very close to an RER train station.Free Internet was useful, especially when I got very sick during my stay (nothing to do with the hotel!) and needed to check symptoms online, communicate with my health care at home, and order a wheelchair at the airport. The room we had was large by Parisian standards with two firm single beds and an immaculate roomy bathroom.Staff is multi-lingual and very helpful; you are steps from the Metro, and it isn't a tourist-ridden area--we didn't see a single Rick Steves book all week! Strongly recommend for a comfortable well-priced place to stay.

<Author>kkotcher
<Content>Charming hotel, great location I found the hotel to be charming and the staff was friendly and helpful. We had room 21 -- we took a room without a view because we needed a bigger room for a family of three (full bed plus a rollaway). The rollaway was the most comfortable portable bed I have ever slept on! The bathroom was huge: we moved a table and chair in there and used it for hanging out at night when you woke up from jet lag and couldn't get back to sleep, but didn't want to wake the others!The room was insulated from the street noise, but the radiator pipes could be pretty noisy at night. I guess this would be my only complaint-- earplugs and Ambien solved this problem for me.I loved the location: lots of restaurants, cafes, metro stops, etc. nearby. Paris Opera House and Galleries Lafayette just 3 blocks away. There's a wonderful little wine bar across the street called La Garonne, and a bakery half a block away where we got breakfast every am (cost 1 euro compared to the 10 euro breakfast at the hotel-- great if you don't want to eat a large breakfast).We had a wonderful experience -- mom, 11 year old child, and grandma all in agreement.

<Author>satchel
<Content>C'est Fantastique! Every morning, I'd soak in the hot tub (we didn't have one of the great big bathrooms, but ours was super clean and had a towel warmer, hair dryer, nice deep tub  shower) and listen to the bells of Trinite chime- it was so relaxing before a day of checking out Paris, and I SO miss it. . .Anyhow, the place was great. We were there the last week of February, and the room I had requested months before was available (64) and we got it (they had emailed back they couldn't guarantee a room, but they remembered!) Each evening we could see the lit up spires of Sacre Coeur in the distance, outside the big double door windows, as we sat and drank champagne at the table in the room. I tell you, though- the housekeeper let us check out some other rooms (I'm nosy) over the course of our stay, when people had checked out, and there were many wonderful rooms, suites, etc.- when we go back (my husband will read this, I hope, and get the hint!) we'll happily stay in any of them.The folks working there were all excellent- we got recommendations for incredible restaurants (try Chez Jean if you want a great, dress-up nouvelle cuisine evening). They'd call for reservations, help us with directions, and all with a friendly smile. The housekeeper was very sweet, complimenting our very little french, leaving the champagne glasses (we got a couple at a small shop down the road) set out on a spiffy doily for their next use (Galleries Lafayette's gourmet section has wonderful demi bottles of champagne that are very nice when chilled in the room fridge!) and even giving me a brief hug when she saw how miserable I looked that last morning, at the thought of going home. . .Now, for the silly stuff- I had bought earplugs because of people complaining about noise here on tripadvisor (we never opened them), and on the first night, when the room was a little warm, we turned down the thermostat and twisted the radiator closed a bit- and didn't have a problem after. The bed was comfortable (and the linen had this wonderful fresh smell that was almost as relaxing as the bath every morning), the big antique armoire had, if you were inclined to want to use them (I wasn't) locks for the door and two of the drawers inside- and held all our stuff. Everything was very charming, very memorable, very when can we come back??I don't like big, impersonal chain hotels very much- I much prefer small bed  breakfast type places, and I thought Hotel Langlois, and the folks who run it, were wonderful.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Hotel Theft---Management Deception We just got back from our stay in Hotel Langlois, and had such a miserable experience that I feel I have to share it with other travelers. Our hotel room was robbed during our stay and the hotel managed this incident very poorly. Our almost entire wardrobe got stolen during the trip including many luxury brand items that you cannot necessarily fit into a safe. Some of these items were bought during their trip in Paris including luxury handbags and footwear. The robbery took place on the day before our departure. We are still investigating the matter, but we have not been compensated for our loss to this day and it seems like such an expensive stay for a 2-star hotel when you factor in our loss, not to mention the stress factor. I would stay away by all means. Here is a recap of the hotel theft incident:We entered the room one evening to find it all messed up and realized many of our belongings were missing from the room. We called the reception which then informed the manager. The manager apologized and told us they would compensate us for whatever was stolen. We said we would like to inform the authorities and make an official statement to the police. The manager told us this is unnecessary and asked us to make a list of stolen items. When we asked the manager if he could see in the computer any entries to our room other than housekeeping, we were told that there were none. However, one hotel staff did tell us later that our room was entered after the housekeeping left and before we arrived. We were puzzled. The next day, when we provided the manager with the total value of the missing goods, he proceeded to the closest bank and came back with a copy of a swift message for X Euros (total value of the stolen items) showing that this amount was transferred to our bank account and allowing no arguments or discontent on our part. The case seemed to be settled and closed. That day, we flew to London, relieved. When we came back home, we found out that the manager recalled the money from our bank without even informing us. We were told to deal with the insurance company. Well, as the hotel manager had told us at the time of the incident that it was unnecessary to call the police and issue an official statement, we were in no position to recover the total value of the goods from the insurance company. We had a wrong start. Had the hotel manager not provided us with the bank receipt showing X euros were transferred to our account the next day, our approach would have been more professional and official. We have been robbed and later deceived by the hotel management. We faced tremendous stress in dealing with this hotel theft situation. The hotel's management of the situation was far more stressful for us than the incident itself. Again, I would stay away by all means. After all, a vacation is meant to bring you peace and not stress.  
<Date>Feb 8, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>No better for the price or more This is simply the best hotel deal in Paris. Yes, the floors will have some creaks and unevenness. No, the rooms will not be absolutely quiet. And, yes, the furniture shows some age.But what some people consider drawbacks, others consider advantages. We stayed in the second floor (third floor for Americans) suite for over a week and found it a perfect place to come home to after a day of museums, stores, or gloriously aimless wandering. We came home to two large rooms with very high ceilings, marble mantels, some charming sculpture, two balconies, and--most of all--comfort. The hotel staff was friendly and helpful; the maid was an absolute charmer. If you want a slick hotel where all the staff is perfectly fluent in English, go elsewhere. If you can manage a bit of French and want to stay someplace where it feels completely like Paris, and if you want to do it at an unbeatable price, stay at the Hotel Langlois.

<Author>le juif errant
<Content>Wonderful Hotel but Clangy Pipes at Night This is a difficult review to write, because the hotel was excellent on almost every level--larger than average room and bathroom for the price, friendly and helpful clerks (with the exception of a dour one at nighttime), close proximity to the Trinite metro, and free Internet access. <Author>badly1004
<Content>Brilliant! We stayed here from 3rd - 5th January and find it very hard to fault the place. First of all the location is superb. To get there we just got off the bus from Beauvais at Port Maillot where we went round the corner to the Metro station and bought our 3 day tickets. From Port Maillot we travelled on to Concorde where we changed for Trinite. Although we took a wee while to find the hotel it's really very easy to find if you know where to look. Just come up the steps of Trinite Metro and take the street on your right - Rue St. Lazare. It's just along there a bit. From this station you can get anywhere within minutes. It's also within easy walking distance of the Moulin Rouge and the Opera.The hotel itself is very charming and we found the service to be excellent. The bed could be more comfortable but the room was huge and we had a shower, toilet, minibar and tv. We were lucky enough to have a room at the back so we didn't get much noise although it's in the middle of a big city so you should probably be prepared for that. Any time we asked for help at the reception we received it with a smile. My biggest tip would be to ask for a restaurant recommendation. You won't be disappointed.All in all if you want a place to rest your head for a decent price in the centre of Paris you can't really go wrong with this place.

<Author>Abby-m
<Content>Not quite impressed I think one has to acknowledge from the very onset that what is good for one will not necessarily be for another. Like other people, I chose the hotel based on good reveiws but I must say I was disappointed. Except for the location and some helpful members of staff, in particular one very friendly and extremely helpful young lady, there isn't much that I liked about the hotel especially the room - from the decor to just the ambiance. Although the room was bigger than most of the hotel rooms I've seen or stayed at in Europe, I did not quite like it. The room was not sound proofed, making each and every sound from other rooms very audible including footsteps on a creaky wooden floor from the room above. I'm sure the occupant of the room below me also suffered, as my floor also creaked badly and I was restless for most of the time. I should maybe take some responsibility for not specifically asking for a non-smoking room, but it was as if people on my floor were on a smoking holiday. They would smoke until the small hours of the morning and by day break I would be literally choking. The bed was uncomfortable, 'caved in' and creaky, the pillows equally uncomfortable. I don't know if the heating system was not effective or if it was just me freezing. The lift is quite antique and intersting but it wasn't getting to my floor on some days.I think some travellers will still find the hotel ok, but personally I don't think I'll be returning.

<Author>Scott&Stacey
<Content>You Can Do Better in Paris We stayed here 5 nights in mid December and we were going to return for 4 nights around New Years, but canceled our reservation and booked elsewhere. There were 3 major problems: the noise, the neighborhood, and --most importantly -- the poor value based on what you can find elsewhere.As for the noise, the sewage pipes and the radiator pipes are not insulated, so you hear every time someone in a nearby room flushes the toilet or showers. But the radiator pipes were the worst. Every night from 10pm to about 2am the pipes from the radiator clanged so loud it was impossible to sleep (even for a heavy sleeper), then the heat would be reduced and the room was chilled during the day. We asked to change rooms, but were told that it was an old system and that other guests had the same complaints and that there was nothing to be done. Don't expect to go to sleep any time prior to 2am because the radiator pipes will keep you awake.Furthermore, the hotel is not in a nice or convenient neighborhood. It's in a busy commercial district. You'll take the metro more than you need to and walk on ugly streets to get where you need to be. It's not the impression you want of Paris.Regarding the value, the Langlois is charging 110 euro for a standard double plus 9 euro for breakfast. So for 2 people, you're paying 128 euro because despite what other guests say, the breakfast is the best deal you'll find. You'll pay 9 - 12,50 euro plus tip for a similar breakfast on the street unless you get a pastry and coffee, which is neither healthy nor adequate for a morning of sightseeing. The 9 euro for a breakfast that includes yoghurt, cheese, and other sources of protein is reasonable. So 128 euro for a noisy, shabby room (We had one of the rooms pictured on the web. It's not so nice in person: terrible mattress, musty smell, and rickety furniture.), a poor location, and a not very helpful staff. Whereas we moved to the Hotel D'Angleterre, on Rue de Jacob in the St. Germain area and for 145 euro (which included breakfast) we had a charming room with a garden/courtyard view, easy walking distance to all the major sights (NOT METRO --the fares add up, by the way), a charming neighborhood that was a pleasure to stroll through, easy access to all sorts of cafes and bistros, a wonderfully helpful staff, a beautifully appointed lounge and breakfast room with lovely china (extensive buffet breakfast), and most importantly, a quiet peaceful place to sleep.Had we not moved hotels, we would have left Paris with a bad impression based on being tired and having to negotiate the horrible streets around the Langlois. It is a budget hotel charging mid-range hotel prices and at these prices, you can find accommodation that is much better and will make your stay in Paris much nicer.  
<Date>Jan 3, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Worst European hotel experience we've ever had! My husband and I just returned from a 7 night stay at the Hotel Langlois. We have relied on TripAdvisor for choosing many of the hotels we have stay in in Europe and we鈥檝e always been satisfied. But the Hotel Langlois was definitely an exception.We made reservations for a superior double with a large bathroom, but when we arrived, we were given a very small room with a tiny bathroom and angled ceiling on the 6th floor. The mattress was visibly and significantly caved in the middle. We were shocked to say the least. We explained that this is not what was represented and asked if they had any rooms like those pictured on their website. Fortunately, they had two others and let us look at both of them. Both were on the 1st floor and were spacious and attractive like those pictured. But one of them again had a mattress that was visibly caved in the middle and was on the street side, with very loud traffic noise even through the closed windows. We chose the other, mostly because it looked like it had an okay mattress (though very worn) and was quieter. We were content with our choice: two big dressers to put our clothes in, a large bathroom, attractive, and typically Parisian. Unfortunately, we discovered that even though this bed wasn鈥檛 visibly caved, it was in reality caved, lumpy, and extremely uncomfortable. As another reviewer wrote, it also got unbearably hot with the heaters and we were forced to keep the windows open which caused the radiators to crackle and pop very loudly all night long. Being on the first floor, we could also feel the room rattle every time the metro train went by, which was quite frequently. By the next morning, we were exhausted, having slept very little. Then when it came time for showers, there was almost no water coming out of the shower head, not even enough to get the shampoo out (my husband worked on it for a while and it got better but was still quite bad)鈥攕o forced to take baths and wash hair under the running faucet. This continued for the first four nights of our visit. We had scheduled a trip to London in the middle of our Paris trip (thank God!!) and by the time it came to leave, we couldn鈥檛 have been happier to check out. Fortunately the hotel we stayed in in London was very nice (and cheaper) with excellent beds, and we were finally able to get some sleep.Upon our return, we were given a room on the 6th floor with a completely disfigured mattress鈥攕ignificant mountains and valleys all over. I鈥檝e honestly never seen anything like it. The room was also small with a bathroom so small that only one of us could stand in it at a time (and this was a superior double!). They had no other room to give us, it was late Christmas Eve, and since we hadn鈥檛 researched anywhere else to stay, we agreed to stay. We flipped the mattress which made it somewhat better. We slept awful again with the same heat and mattress problems, but this time in addition we had extremely loud plumbing noises that sounded like a waterfall coming into our bathroom every time someone flushed the toilet. By the next morning we figured out what was going on鈥攖here literally was a waterfall coming into our bathroom. Some of the pipes were broken and every time someone flushed the toilet their raw sewage was pouring onto our bathroom floor. At this point, I felt pretty resigned to dealing with it and just getting through the next three days, but my husband was so horrified (Thank God) that he demanded another room. The entire time we were there, the staff was overwhelmingly UNhelpful, but this time there was a different person at the desk that my husband spoke to. She was very sympathetic and offered to give us a suite for the price of a superior double. We moved into the suite on the 3rd floor鈥攁gain another mattress with visible caving in the middle. The bathroom had an awful smell of urine, the TV was broken, the room was overheated, and filled up with exhaust fumes in the morning when the windows were open. By our last night, at about 3:00 am, my husband pulled out one of the chairs that turns into a twin bed and exclaimed, 鈥淥h my God, it鈥檚 actually comfortable!鈥?br/>A word about the staff: with the exception of one person (a young woman who spoke excellent English and was very kind), the staff was pretty much completely unwilling to help. A month before our stay I contacted the hotel and asked them if they would be able to help with recommendations for Christmas dinner since from what I could tell most restaurants would be closed that day. The woman I spoke to told me it was too early to ask and told me to contact them two weeks before Christmas. So I emailed them two weeks before and was told that they would provide that information when we arrived. When we arrived, my husband asked the older woman (not the young helpful one) at the desk and she said she didn鈥檛 have any recommendations to give us. Then when we asked again upon our return on Christmas Eve, the man at the desk said he had nothing to recommend. I explained that we really needed help with this and that they agreed to help. I asked him if he would be willing to do some research and find out what was open. The man had the gall to tell me to go research it on my own on their computer! I told him that I had already spent several hours on the internet trying to find something but was not successful because I didn鈥檛 speak the language, and didn鈥檛 know the city and what resources to look at. He said, 鈥淲ell whatever I find you could just find yourself.鈥?I said to him very assertively, 鈥淣o, it鈥檚 appropriate for you to do this. It鈥檚 part of your job. When we return from dinner, I expect you to have this information鈥?Very quickly, he had a restaurant and made reservations for us. Why was it necessary for us to go through that?I also emailed the hotel prior to our stay asking for help with getting Louvre tickets. I said that I had heard that you can avoid the long lines by purchasing the tickets in advance, and asked if they had tickets themselves (a common service of most concierges) or had a way of getting them. I received a very terse and rude reply, 鈥淣o, it is not possible for us to go and stand in line for you to get your tickets for you,鈥?and then she wrote the word Louvre in all caps because I had misspelled it. When I received this reply, and being upset enough to want to cancel my reservation, I decided it must have been due to a language barrier and gave them the benefit of the doubt, but having experienced the lack of hospitality there, I now know that it wasn鈥檛.My husband and I have stayed in many hotels throughout Europe and South America at comparable or cheaper prices, and I can honestly say that this is the worst hotel experience we have ever had. Some of the rooms are spacious and attractive and it is in a very convenient location, but unless they buy new mattresses and undergo some significant renovations (heaters, plumbing, etc) and hire new staff that is actually interested in helping, I cannot possibly recommend this hotel. Having gone through the experience, although I never would have imagined saying it, I would recommend staying at a cookie-cutter, boring Ibis for a comparable or cheaper rate. At least there you鈥檒l get some sleep.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Hotel, Great Location Having visited Paris five times previously, staying in hotels at around the 100 euro mark, I believe that the Hotel Langlois, represents the best value for money that I have experienced in Paris.We stayed over Xmas and paid 96 euros per night. The rooms are clean and pleasantly decorated with antiques, and our bathroom had recently been renovated.Staff are very helpeful (confirming dinner reservations, making restaurant recomendations, and printing directions and metro information).The hotel is in an excellent location, only a 5 min walk from Opera. The Metro stop Trinite is less than a two minute walk away.A taxi stand is located at the end of the street (approx 5 euros to Gare de Nord Station, 9 euros to St. Germain, 7 euros to Champs Eleysee).There is also a fantastic Bistro called Le Bistro des Deux Theatres near the hotel, at 18, rue Blanche. Turn left outside the hotel, and then take first street on your right - continue for about 200m and you will hit rue Blanche. We had dinner here on Xmas Eve, and it was one of the best meals we had in Paris (33 euros for champagne cocktail, 3 course meal, bottle of wine and coffee!!!)Hotel Langois, is NOT a 5 star hotel, but if you are looking for a hotel in an excellent location, that is clean and great value - you really can't beat Hotel Langlois. I thoroughly recommend it.

<Content>Good value and great location Like many people, we booked this hotel because of the reviews it has received. We weren't disappointed, especially in view of the price we paid (96 Euros per room per night, for a double) and my experience of other Paris hotels in this price bracket.Most of the comments in the other reviews are true: large rooms, very nice decor, and attention to detail. Unfortunately the bathroom size seems to depend on the amount you pay - our room was in the low end of the price bracket and we had a tiny bathroom! It was nice and clean, but basically wouldn't do for 'larger' people!One more thing to flag up: it is an old building and has very thin walls, as well as creaky floorboards. On one night the heating was on quite high I think, with the result that the old radiator in our room was making a banging noise for quite a few hours. It didn't bother us much as we'd packed earplugs, but there's no way we could have slept through it otherwise!All in all I'd definitely stay at the Hotel Langlois again - you're not going to find a hotel with as much charm and individuality for the price in Paris. Just remember to take some earplugs if you're anything but a heavy sleeper...!  
<Date>Dec 15, 2005
