<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Gem Of A Hotel A lovely hotel in a great location - the nearest Metro stop is Trinite which is only a few steps from the hotel and from there you can be in any part of the city in a very short time. The hotel is also only 5 minutes walk away from Blvd Haussman where you will find some of the major Paris department stores including Printemps and Galleries Lafeyette.Overall the hotel was clean and the staff were friendly and welcoming. The rooms are large and traditionally French (from the era of the Belle Epoche) and the rate per night is very reasonable. I would have no hesitation in recommending the Hotel Langlois no matter what the purpose of your trip, be it business or pleasure.

<Author>JackTheTraveller
<Content>Lovely and convenient but not outstanding This is a nice hotel in a very good location, close to the big department stores, a few nice brasseries, and very close to the subway. To accomodate 2 relatively grown up children, we reserved a suite and got the one on the 4th floor, facing the street. We were also offered a studio on the 7th floor but decided not to try it. The room was very nice and clean and fairly large by Paris standards. One of our problems was that the heat worked too well and we needed to open the window but the street was so noisy that we had to close it. So during the nights, we played open/close the window to maintain a relatively normal temperature in the room and to reduce the dryness. The breakfast is a bit expensive for what they offer. There is a computer available to use and to check email and that is very convenient. The reception is receptive. We used a taxi from CDG back and forth and paid about 50 Euros each way for 4 people and 3 suitcases. Due to the noise level, I would not return to the hotel during the summer months but would consider it in the winter. BTW, the prices mentioned in TripAdvisor are not realisitic. Rooms are much more expensive, about 100 euros is the minimun you are likely to pay.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the lift! Good value 2 star hotel ideally located only 100 metres from a metro stop and 5 mins walk from the La Fayette and Printemps department stores and the Opera.The hotel is over 100 years old and that adds to the charm. It is full of antiques but also has the modern touches eg free broadband internet access in the lobby. The rooms vary in size we stayed in 24 which had two separate rooms - a double bed in one and two single sofa beds in the other.The floor creaks, there is the occasional distant rumble from the metro, the shower runs hot and cold but that all adds to the charm of the hotel.Continental breakfast costs 9 euro and is reasonably priced compared to surrounding cafe's. Staff friendly and speak good English.The lift is straight out of a thriller movie - we were only on the second floor but my wife insisted that we used the lift every time.The Hotel Langlois (Des Croises) thoroughly deserves it's high rating on Tripadvisor. I'm glad we didn't go for a soulless modern Ibis or Comfort hotel for the same price.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wish we could have stayed longer!!! We loved it!!! We chose to stay here based on the Trip Advisor reviews, and it lived up to everyone's high remarks! We absolutely loved it! For the price, you cannot beat this hotel! Our honeymoon was 2 weeks long, 6 of those nights in Paris (4 at the beginning of the trip at a different hotel, 2 in the end of the trip at the Langlois), and we chose a slightly cheaper hotel for the first 4 nights. I wish we had stayed in this hotel the whole time! It was so cute and really very charming. I loved this location. At first, I looked at a map and thought that it looked like it was slightly far from the monuments, but it really isn't! And not to mention the fact that the metro stop is SO close...just at the end of the street! There are so many little restaurants close to the hotel and there is a great little wine shop just across and down the street towards the church (the owner of the wine shop is so nice and spoke great English). The hotel is also very close to Au Printemps and Galleries Lafayette (shopping). Also, there is a great little creperie near the metro stop. The room that we had was great. It was on the 5th floor and had a great view of the street and the huge church/cathedral (not sure???) and the tops of the buildings. We loved the room. It was very very big by Parisian standards, and it was just very comfortable! Again....we loved it!From reading a couple of other reviews, I noticed something that I strongly disagree with, not about the hotel itself, but rather getting to the hotel. I read that the other reviewers only paid about 40 Euros for a taxi ride to the hotel, but we took a taxi for one leg of our airport travels to and from Paris city center. We were charged 60 Euros for 2 people with 3 suitcases. We knew that we were being majorly ripped off, but we couldn't do anything about it. The other 3 legs of our airport traveling, we used a company called Airport Connection, (you have to pre-book them over the internet) and we loved them. Don't book them if you expect a super-quick trip (it takes aprx 45 mins-1 hour to Paris from the airport  vice versa), but they are reliable and have the cheapest price I could find anywhere! Their website is ----------. We loved their service. =)Overall, I just absolutely loved this hotel and the neighborhood it was situated in. The true testament is to ask Would I stay there again? and the answer is without a doubt YES! Stay there....you won't be disappointed!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Value for Money I stayed in Hotel Langlois with my family on the 5 to 10 Nov. We stayed in room 14 on the first night, no air-con and it was noisy even with the lightest traffic. We requested to stay at the top floor and was given the change the next night. Room 64 was great, bigger than room 14 and noise level was lower. The bed was ok however the pillows were too soft. The hotel is warm and cosy with friendly staff. The room is clean and tidy. The staffs are helpful and they speak english. Hotels are very expensive in Paris, and for the price I have paid for , I would say this hotel offers great value for money.It was our first trip to Paris, we managed to find our ways around the city. Most of the musesums and monuments can be reached using the metro. You will find bakeries, cafes, chinese food down the streets. Taxi trip from the hotel to CDG airport cost abt 40 euros.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Everything as promised! It's comforting to know that Tripadvisor ratings are reliable, and the Hotel des Croises certainly lived up to its ratings when we visited in early October. The staff in this delighful hotel were quietly courteous and efficient. They offered a very helpful service, which included some assistance that went well beyond the minimalist approach often adopted in modern hotels. Enough has been said about the unique charms of this establishment in other postings:they are all true! The room size was exceptional,and the room rate offered quite stunning value for money.This is not a luxury hotel, but offers much that one would not expect in this price range. Another attractive feature of a stay here is the accessibility of the location. Only one minute's walk from The Metro, we reached the hotel in only 20 minutes from the airport bus terminus; the major sights are all within a short Metro ride and made easier with a tourist transport pass which was well worth buying.There are limitless eating places, and even if you head for the Left Bank, you may eat well within even the tightest budget.We have no decision to make when we next head for Paris; we shall be staying at the Hotel des Croises.

<Author>westwing
<Content>Great 2 Star Hotel This is our 5th time in Paris. We have stayed at 5 star and 2 star hotels. All hotels in Paris have a star rating from 1 to 5 based on a complex formula of ammenities and location. Hotel Langlois if rated 2 strs but is closer to a 3 star. It is very clean and the rooms are extremely large for Paris. Breakfast is served in a small room off the main lobby. Cost is 9 Euros. Not many tabels and very warm. The food is OK at best. You can get a full American breakfast for 12.50 (eggs, bacon, pastry, potatoes, coffee and juice) at one of the 4 cafes in the main square (3 minute walk).The lower rooms and rooms on the street side of St Lazare are very noisy. Our room #12 did not have A/C and when you open the window, the noise is extreme. We also had room #15 and this was a little quieter but smaller. Staff friendly and speaks english. The Metro is a quick 4 minute walk. If this is your first time in Paris the Metro is a wonderful transit system that will take you anywhere in central Paris in a matter of minutes. Very easy to understand. Beds and pillows are comfortable. Decor is very nice with accent on old French. Walls, paintings, furniture bed looked great but the lamps, TV, minibar and bathroom toiletries were more likely bought at a Kmart type store. No clock but wakeup service. Bathroom in our room was BIG and CLEAN. If you like a HOT shower take it before 8:30 or at night.The shower curtain was very cheap and the water pressure OK. Taxi from Charles De Gaulle airport cost 42 Euros (50 with 4 people). Roissy Bus from airport will drop you off at the Opera (9 euros each)which is a short walk to the hotel. If you have never been before be warned that the sidewalks in this area are very crowded so it's tough with luggage. Hotel is also close to MAJOR department stores of Au Printemps and Gallieries Layafatte. If you have time check out the window displays at these stores. Remarkable! We went in November and each winodw was a magical event with full animation.We all enjoyed this hotel. Best features are the cleanliness, price and size of rooms. Worst feature--street noise. All in all, if you are on a tight budget and want a CLEAN hotel in a great part of the city, this is a good buy.  
<Date>Nov 8, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>FANTASTIC!!! We loved it! We stayed at the Hotel Langlois for 6 nights in early October/05 and just loved it. It is affordable, clean, quiet, and oozes old-world charm. Our room was on the 6th floor facing St-Lazare avenue and we had a great view of the nearby cathedral St-Trinite. The single elevator is funky and fun to ride and likely dates back to the original construction of the hotel.The staff at the Hotel are very friendly and willing to let you try your French out - it helps that they know some English (the manager is very good at English). Breakfast is a reasonable cost and is pretty good, but we suggest you go explore the nearby cafes for your petit-dejeuner. Having said that, we ate breakfast a number of times at the hotel as it was very convenient.The location is great - just 50 feet or so to the Metro stop, and from there Paris is very easy to explore. For those who have been to Paris before, you know how important it is to be close to the Metro. The Metro stop is St-Strinite on line #12 and you can easily transfer to other lines that take you to all the major attractions like the Louvre, Eiffel Tower, and Notre Dame. Tip: ask the Metro ticket booth person for a grand plan de Metro (map) as it is the easiest metro map to follow.The Gare du Nord (Paris North Station) is a 10-euro taxi ride, which was great for us since we chunneled to London after Paris.For food, there are numerous cafes and restaurants in the area. We loved the crepe stand across from St Trinite cathedral for a quick snack, the bakery just down the street, and the cafe on the corner. Tip: DO NOT eat at the Greek sandwich shop on St Lazare across from the Hotel. Their service was terrible and the food was expensive and very bland.If we ever go back to Paris, we will likely stay here again.  
<Date>Oct 9, 2005

<Author>EuropeanAmerican
<Content>Very Happy with the Hotel Langlois My wife and I stayed at the Hotel Langlois from Sept 24th through Sept 29th 2005. I did a lot of research through Tripadvisor and I am pleased with our choice for the hotel. The positives you read in the other reviews are true. I was mainly impressed by the staff, specifically the two young women who staff the front desk. They were very helpful when we had questions about where to find a store to buy food for a picnic (the Galleries Lafayette has a gourmet food section), where to find a laundry (walk out the front door of the Hotel, take a right and it's a 5 minute walk on St. Lazare and is on the right) and how to find the Hard Rock Cafe' - Paris (it's on Boulevard Hausmann - we only went there for a souvenier for a friend). I'd also like to put in a plug for the guys at the panini / crepe stand attached to the Royal Trinite' cafe. The panini's are great (try the l'espangnol) and the cooks are really friendly.

<Author>WindshearDon
<Content>Great Value, Good Location We stayed at Hotel Langlois based on reviews found on TripAdvisor. It exceeded all our expectations. We wanted a quiet place which was well-situated for a brief visit in Paris while we got over our jet lag. It offered a lot more.We were able to get to the hotel by train from Aeroport Charles de Gaulle easily (40 mins) and quickly with our bags in tow. The hotel's location is between Opera Garnier and Montmarte on a quiet and safe street. The Metro is 50 steps away. It is near all the big department stores and has some nice cafes in the neighbourhood. The hotel's rooms are huge by European standards and some of the bathrooms (we were travelling with friends) are enormous by any standard. In the middle of summer - the air conditioning (remote controlled) was very efficient and QUIET! Their is also a small fridge in each room. The beds are great and cleaning staff keep the rooms immaculate. The buffet continental breakfast is quite nice and is not exhorbitantly priced compared to the cafes. The elevator is a wonderful relic that will hopefully stay in service for many more decades. Reception was friendly and efficient. There is also an internet computer available to guests (except during breakfast).The downside is that there are very limited views and limited service in the hotel. The halls are a bit musty and the TVs are small with only a dozen channels.If you came to Paris to enjoy getting out on the city and want a hotel offering great value (110 euros per room) and a sound sleep then this is it. You can spend your savings on great restaurants instead! By the way - try Deux Theatres - a five minute walk from Hotel Langlois.  
<Date>Sep 12, 2005

We stayed in a suite that accomodated us well, but for the last night needed two seperate rooms since I made a mistake when I reserved. They did give us two rooms, moved our luggage for us, and gave us a very much coveted air-conditioned room! When I checked out and paid for our stay, I realized that they only charged us for the suite again for the last night! That saved a bit of money. I doubt that there is a better deal in Paris. In the neighborhood we picked up outstanding coissants for 1 euro. Breakfast for 1 euro? My children voted their stay in Paris the best of our 2 week adventure.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Lovely hotel, lovely stay. Hotel Langlois is a Parisian gem. The staff was very helpful and kind, the room was tastefully appointed and relatively quiet (no street noise and minimal noise from other rooms). The location is perfect and the price moderate. The computer in the lobby with Internet access was a big help to us. The bathtub in our room was perfect for a long, hot bubble bath to sooth our travel-weary bodies.We also took advantage of what the surrounding neighborhood had to offer: the sandwich and pastry shops for breakfast and lunch, a self-service laundry just down the street, a corner sidewalk-cafe for sitting and watching the world rush past. With the metro, bus stop and taxi stand close by, we found this the hotel a convenient base from which to explore the city. AND it is within walking distance of shopping along Boulevard Hausmann: Printemps, the Galleries Lafayette and Marks  Spencer.Yes, the hotel has its imperfections, but they only add to the quaint charm of this Parisian experience. We were there to see Paris and when we returned to our room at the Hotel Langlois each night we slept very well indeed!

<Author>Sparkley
<Content>Wonderfully romantic Hotel Langlios I booked Hotel langlois based solely on the previous reviews from Tripadvisor and I was not disappointed.The trip to Paris was a surprise for my husband for our first wedding anniversary. Hotel Langlois was perfect. I requested about 5 months in advance to have one of the rooms on the top floor and although they wouldn't guarantee it we did get one. The room had it's own balcony from which you coud see the Sacre Couer and we had our own little table for two in front of it. The hotel is very quaint, it has an old style lift with two doors (if you don't close it after you the lift won't go and pick anyone else up!)All in all, I have very high standards but I hate paying over the odds. I could not fault Hotel Langlois - fabulous hotel and incredibly good value. I will certainly be reccommending it to all my friends and I will definitely return myself.

<Author>CADreamin
<Content>Wonderful Find in Paris!!! After many weeks of searching through various opinion-based web sites, I booked the Hotel Langlois for a four night stay in May. What an absolutely charming little hotel!! Our room was on the fourth floor and furnished in the art deco style. The bathroom was almost as big as the bedroom and extremely well equipped. While our room was located at the back of the hotel, it was very quiet and had wonderful breezes coming through the three very large windows (which was nice because we were there during a mini-heat wave that Europe was experiencing). The staff was exceptionally friendly and most everyone spoke English. The breakfast, at first, seemed a little pricey; however, after checking out many of the local eateries, my husband declared that it was actually a pretty good deal. Hotel Langolis is located near the metro and rail stop which was a very big plus since we were traveling Europe by train. Would we recommend it to friends/family: YES! Would we stay there again? YES!!!!!

<Author>co9222
<Content>Wonderful Hotel We have just returned from a weeks stay at the Hotel Langlois (July 15-22, 2005). It was a perfect hotel for us; a quiet neighborhood that became a sanctuary after the jam-packed sightseeing days, pleasant staff, very tastefully decorated common rooms with a wonderful little elevator, a comfortable bedroom with a quiet, remote-controlled air-conditioning unit, great thick towels in the bathroom, a view of Sacre Coeur, and even free internet access. The neighborhood provided all our needs--a quick half block to the Metro, two banks with ATM access within a half block, a post office a half block away, a little Brasserie for coffee and croissants in the morning (and even a decent dinner at night if you are too exhausted to return to the touristy areas) right next to the Metro entrance, a nice little patisserie, and only a few blocks from the renowned Galleries Lafayette Department Stores (foodies--you need to see the Galleries Lafayette Gourmet Foods department!) All in all, we were thrilled with this little hotel in the ninth arrondissement and will certainly return to it when we return to Paris.

<Author>babygame
<Content>Met Expectations - Good Staff Recommendations Stayed here July 1-3, 2005. Nice location (close to Trinity church) and excellent staff. Gave us great recommendations on nearby restaurant (Restaurant of 2 Theaters, just around corner, 32 Euros priced fixed for champagne, wine, and 3-course meal with many excellent choices), where to boat the Seine from (Eiffel Tower - we picked boat with shortest line), where to buy food (nearby convenience store), and how to get to CDG (Roussy bus at Opera). Only shortcomings - even with the fan - the room was hot! We had just missed a major heat wave in the City so I can only imagine what previous week was like (bad). We had view across alley of an office type building (room 32); luckily they were gone for rest of our stay. Also, on Sat. and Sun. the nearby Patissierie is closed. On Sunday, almost everything is closed so plan ahead. We didn't breakfast at the hotel, so cannot comment on that. Did smell the food cooking early in the morning!! Thoroughly enjoyed our stay and would go here again.

<Author>Romancinparis
<Content>Charming hotel, close to sights. My husband and I stayed at this hotel for four nights in the beginning of June and we had a great time. I would stay there again. This is a basic, friendly, clean hotel, perfect for a quick break. If you want more luxury you have to pay a higher price. Roissy Bus is best way to get from CDG to this hotel, pick up right outside airport and drop off a short walk from hotel for 8.50 euros single journey. The TA price is out of date we stayed in a basic room and it cost 96 euros probably not as good value as it used to be but we thought a fair price for what you get. The entrance is lovely and evocative of a traditional Parisian hotel yet has modern facilities, free Internet access was useful, the reception staff is very helpful, they booked restaurants by phone for us and helped advise best routes for our planned outings. Our room had a view of the back of buildings, which was very ugly, but then we did not go to Paris to spend our time in our room admiring the view. It had air con which was nice when it got hot and a mini fridge that we used to store drinks and snacks. We did not have the hotel breakfast as we thought it was quite expensive but bought snacks from the stalls around Trinite d Estenne d Orves (local metro stop) or did breakfast at a self serve caf茅 on Champs Elysees 4.90 euro.The metro is defiantly the way to travel around Paris we bought a 3-day Visite Pass and did so many trips. Louvre is the place to see, take the metro and get off at palais royal musee du louvre we found it the quickest way in less waiting in line than entrance over ground.For the romantics I can highly recommend a dinner cruise on the Bateaux Parisiens lovely food, live music, dancing under the lights of Eiffel Tower and beautiful scenery what more do you need.

<Content>Memorable -appealing- place ! Hotel Langlois is a memorable place - evoking the experience of Parisian hotels of numbers of decades ago--except that now (and not then !), prviate baths are present.The small lobby, old evelvator, rooms with 'mixed decor' of furnishings, and tall shuttered windows overlooking the courtyard will remind some of their earlier times in Paris, and for others, offer the present-day experience, which one is glad still exists.In addition, the service is very good. Helpful - and patient- staff respond to requests for assistance/advice.One hopes that this hotel does not respond to the pressures of 'moderniation' and 'updates' that would essentially rob it of its appeal and charm.

<Author>LindaAustralia
<Content>Are we talking about the same hotel??? I too recently stayed in Room #31 as part of an 8 week trip around the world and Hotel Langlois was the worst room hubby and I encountered. True, it was a large room with huge bathroom but the 'antique' furniture for us meant old and broken. One bedside table door and one cupboard door didn't open, the bed creaked terribly (as we know the floor does too) and was a double when we had been confirmed a queen. The 'log' style pillow was very uncomfortable. Acoustics where poor, we were asked to turn down the TV which we did not have up very high. Room was so hot we had to request a fan. There were no tea making facilities. As for the convenience of the metro a few steps away, we could hear the underground trains rumbling by all night! The room is certainly affordable and the staff are very helpful but I would not recommend the hotel.

<Author>DH_Spore
<Content>Charming, good location and huge bathroom Stayed 6 nights at Hotel Langlois from 15 May to 21 May. Would highly recommend this charming hotel. Room #31 was spacious and bathroom huge. Deep bathtub with shower curtains. What was great was that toilet was in a separate room (with door) in the corner of the bathroom. Although room had no view, plus point was that it doesn't face the street and is quiet. We opened the windows at night and didn't have to use the fan which was a tad too strong.We viewed another room before settling for #31. The other room had a much smaller bathroom. Room #31 ws also kind of a stand alone unit and probably quieter as a result. At 96 euros, #31 is a steal for paris.Location was great. A few steps from Trinite Metro station. Ten minutes to most major attractions by metro. Area felt safe (I get scared quite easily :) ) and there were a number of cafes nearby. Galleries was a ten min walk away and gourmet section there for takeaway food is great.My husband and I don't speak french but had no problems with the hotel staff at the reception who all spoke English. I would strongly recommend this hotel!! The charm of the hotel definitely makes up for the creaky floor.

<Author>young_urbanite
<Content>Charming hotel with huge rooms My girlfriend  I stayed here for 4nights last December in a particularly bitter Paris winter. We booked the hotel through its own website and paid on our departure.Langlois is a small hotel, close to Gare St.Lazare. Though not immediately nearby any of the more touristy areas, we often walked to the Louvre and there is enough nearby to keep you going. I would recommend getting a tube to go eat but only for an evening meal, and only because many of Paris' best restaurants are off the beaten track (Try Willy's Wine Bar).We stayed in a second floor room (small lift isn't necessary except for the infirm) without no view. However the room was exceptionally large for the price, with grand antique furnishings and a large clean bathroom (superb deep bath!)The decor may not have been to everyone's taste (redgreen in our room, slightly baroque feel) but I enjoyed it since most cheap hotels have zip character.From memory we did get charged slightly more than the website quoted but given the large comfortable room, friendly service (helps if you have basic French) and reasonable location I doubt many people will leave unhappy.

<Author>bearinthefield
<Content>Let me join the chorus You will not find a better hotel in Paris for the money. We stayed in #31 for 104 Euros. It had a bathroom bigger than ours at home and was quiet, facing the inner courtyard. The floors do creak as others have said, but I will take that as a part of its character over a sterile Ibis or such. It was absolutely clean and the 12 ' ceilings with double french doors to the bathroom were charming. I expected Cary Grant to walk down the carpeted stairs in a dinner jacket or spring out of the tiny cage elevator.The staff was very friendly and helpful (offering us coffee and pastries in the front hall as we waited for our departure taxi, at no expense, and use of the e mail in the office as examples).For balance, the only downside I can find is that it is not a 10-15 minute walk to the major attractions as Notre Dame etc, but that is offset by its proximity to the metro stop, the CDG bus stop etc. Not all of the furniture in the room was old, antique type stuff.If you are looking for an older, affordable classic Paris hotel with style, this is it.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A gem...and very Parisian Okay, we got to Paris after a very long train ride from Amsterdam (a 4-hour-ride that became 7 hours when someone expire on the train), so at 3 a.m. we stumble into the Hotel Langlois. The guy on duty wasn't the friendliest guy in the world, but I think he could see that we weren't up for a lot of small talk...or he could have not spoken any English (who knows). All I could think was, Get me to my room.And our room at Hotel Langlois more than lived up to our hopes. It was furnished with lovely antiques. It had high ceilings. A small terrace. The bathroom was small, but clean and equipped with all the necessities (including a hair dryer). The bathtub was extra-deep. It was everything you hope a Parisian hotel would be, and for the money, it's a steal (but, shhhh, don't tell anyone).We option to not have the breakfast, although the cost is very comparable to anything else you'll find. Fortunately, there is a WONDERFUL pastry shop two doors down.It is in a great, not-too-touristy area of the city. We walked to the Louvre the first day, so you can do that or take the Metro which is a few yards away or a but which is right across the street. How convenient!While the service didn't improve much (the front desk wasn't English-friendly and my husband's French skills were not that helpful), we were very pleased with our stay and are recommending it to our friends and to you.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Bargain This was my first time in Paris and althought I had no other hotels in Paris with which to compare Hotel Langlois, we found the hotel to be very nice. The room was sufficiently roomy and clean. More importantly, however, was the accommodating staff. The staff was very cordial and was always willing to assist us in navigating Paris. Location was excellent. About half a block from the Metro. Near several restaurants and near Prentemps and Galeries Lafayette, two major department stores. Paris is very expensive, primarily because of the present rate of exchange. Consequently, we purchased most of our dinners from local stores in the neighborhood. Further up Rue Saint Lazare are neighborhood stores where you can purchase cheese, wine, meats, bread and fruit. After a full day of sight seeing, we enjoyed buying a bottle of wine, some cheese, salami, fruit and bread and taking it back to the room for a relaxing evening meal. Near the hotel is a very popular bakery where you can purchase breads, prepared quiche and salads. The standard room at 96 Euros is a bargain. For a two-star hotel, I thought it was very nice.

<Author>Wolftrapper
<Content>A charming hotel in a terrific area. The Hotel Langlois is an excellent value. I just returned from staying 5 nights at this hotel. It is located on a quiet street in the 9th district within walking distance of many of the Paris sights. The Metro, city bus, eateries are all very close by and the Roissy Bus, to and from CDG airport, is only a short walk. The staff of the Langlois were all terrific, especially the three women that I met over the 6 days who worked at the front desk. There is a computer with free internet access for guests to use. Because of all the places to eat in Paris, I did not have breakfast at the hotel so I can not speak to that. Rooms were clean and very confortable and as I already said my room was very quiet. I had a room facing the courtyard and was able to keep the windows open whenever I was in the room. This is important to me since many hotels in Paris have rooms facing noisy, busy streets. Another nice feature of this hotel is that the rooms are not all the same. Each has its own style and features. I have stayed at other hotels in Paris, however, when I return the Hotel Langlois will be my first choice.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>High expectations; serious disappointment. After much research (Trip Advisor  every other source we could find) we were thrilled to be able to book three nights for our family of four at the Hotel Langlois. The chance to stay at the #4 rated hotel in all of Paris for a very reasonable price seemed like a wonderful opportunity. We were assigned to the attic apartment where we found our room to be nothing close to the photos and/or room descriptions on the internet. The Hotel Langlois website speaks of Ecole de Nancy furniture  crafted mahogany and sycamore headboards ... Our double bed was a portable bed w/ no headboard, sitting about 6 inches off the ground. I don't believe Ecole de Nancy furniture includes the wicker and particle board pieces in our room. Paint was peeling off the walls in several places. The space had great potential. - It was good-sized (the reason they told us we were placed there). There was a small kitchen. The bathroom was nice. And there was an incredible view of Sacre-Coeur. But it was as though the room was an afterthought. - A place for families when everything else was occupied. Certainly not representative of what I would expect from the #4 hotel in Paris. I would suggest that Hotel Langlois paint  furnish the attic so that it measures up to the rest of their facility. A little work and a small investment would make that space a highlight of a Paris vacation instead of a source of disgust and disappointment.

<Author>gcollins
<Content>Perfect hotel We just returned from 7 nights at this hotel in room 31 which had a double bed and a large bathroom. We had a twin bed added since there were 3 of us. The room was quiet and ample. There was no view, but that was okay. Breakfast was 9 euros which is better than in a restaurant for the food you get, but much easier to walk outside the hotel to the little patisserie close by and get a croissant and orange juice. Good place for lunch! The Trinite metro stop is the nearest one. Being in the 9th makes it a quieter hotel than most, but still convenient to attractions if you use the metro. The staff at the front desk understood English very well. The drinks in the refrigerator in the room are reasonably priced which is unusual for a hotel. I would definitely stay here again. There is computer access in the breakfast room as well. The cost for the room was 110 euros. There was no additional charge for the extra bed/person.

<Author>lasscass
<Content>Large rooms and fabulous views.... If you get one of the top 2 floors, that is. I had high expectations of this hotel, and for the most part those expectations were met, but I had to do some negotiating first, which displeased me. I made my reservation two months in advance, and specifically asked for a street facing room, on one of their higher floors, but apon check in was given room 32, (3rd floor up out of 7 floors) and it was facing a courtyard which was not only dreary but a tad creepy due to the fact that it seems to be some sort of office building and is deserted totally at night. And I adore and require fresh air, and apon thrusting open the windows I noticed that just to the right of the window is pideon central and a TON of guano (pidgeon poo)...so I kept my window shut. But I must say that I immediatly went down to reception and kindly reminded the very nice young lady that my reservation was for a street view room and she told me that they are not able to make an guarantees, and that for today she could not place me in a street view, so I inquired about tommorow and she said they could place me in a street room then, so I was fine with that. And indeed the next day they did infact transfer me into a new room, which was FABULOUS! Room #64 with a beautiful window and railing that looked out far above the buildings across the street and had a fabulous full on view of Sacre Coeur, which is lit up at night. I noticed a fellow lodger posted a few photos, including the view from the room of #63, which was the third window to my left, so I had a clearer view of Sacre Coeur than they did, just for your reference. The bathroom had a great opening window too. There was a nice seating area, which consisted of a table and two chairs. There was also another chair by the heater. The view and fresh air from the window was so nice that a few nights I opted to dine in so to speak, and brought home a hot quiche from a patisserie, and some cheese, wine and various snacks. I really enjoyed staying in room #64. The housekeeping staff were very nice and the reception staff was very nice too, but even with using quite a bit of limited french, there really was a huge communication gap. ( I did order breakfast in my room, over the phone, entirely in french, though lousy, which the lady understood perfectly) but idealy if you spoke fluent french, this is the best. I opted not to ask for directions or help in locating things in town because I knew how difficult it would be for us to understand one another. All in all though, a very pleasant stay, and the staff is willing to accomodate your desires, if you are able to make yourself understood. I highly recommend having your breakfast delivered to your room, and enjoying your view and coffee. A delight! Oh, one other note...the elevator has one large iron door one opens first, and then a pair of wood and rattan inner doors, which can be held open by attaching them to little grabber hooks inside the elevator...anyway, apon exiting the elevator, if you fail to unhook these two inner doors, and just shut the outer iron door, and walk away....the elevator stays on that floor. Forever. Or, untill someone comes along and closes the doors or uses the elevator from that floor. So I did have to walk up 7 flights of stairs TWICE in one day because someone had forgotten to close the doors. The staff never told me about this or that I should pay attention to be sure to close the doors each time I rode the elevator, so I think this is something they should really stress to the guests. A terribly sweet elevator though!! An old Otis sweetie that just goes silently up and down all day. Wooden and tiny. Oh, one more thing...the wooden floors in the rooms are so darn squeeky!! In the first room, #32 it was sooooo bad I felt guilty walking around at all, just knowing how awful it must sound below. But my second room only had one or two spots which were easy to avoid. I'd definately stay at this hotel again only next time I plan on renting an apartment. Have fun, folks!!  
<Date>Mar 27, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great location  Hotel Langlois would have received 5 stars from me if It hadn't been for the fact that we asked to change room. I booked a twin room 7 months in advance of my visit to Paris with my mother for her 75th Birthday  specifically asked for a room with a view. When we arrived we were given a twin room that looked out to a wall and was a bit dingy. Decor was ok, but I was pretty disappointed after reading the rave reviews on tripadvisor and having booked so early with my specific request. The bathroom of the twin room (room 32) was very small and you could quite clearly hear someone splashing around in the bath in the next room.When I asked for an alternative room, the receptionist was very helpful and showed me a number of rooms. There was a small private apartment on the 7th floor with great views, but all modern furniture. Another room had the same view as our twin room but had a double bed  was a bit brighter, but eventually I was shown what I think must have been a suite and that's where we stayed for 3 nights in art nouveau splendour. I was so glad that I had asked to be moved because it made such a difference to our holiday. We had an ornate carved double bed, huge bathroom hidden behind what looked like a cupboard door and our own sitting area. (room 44)Breakfast at 鈧? each for continental seemed a bit steep, so we went to the bakery a few doors away for breakfast for 2 people at 鈧?. Fab, safe location - easy to walk to sacre coeur, opera, boulevard Haussman. Good access to metro  RER stations.I'd gladly stay at the Langlois again, but would specify a room number if possible and even be willing to pay the extra supplement to guarantee a bigger room.

<Author>kmstraveller
<Content>Not bad, good value I stayed here with my wife over a weekend and overall I was pleased. On the plus side the hotel is in a great location. It's close to the RER, Saint Lazare line (just down the street) and it's right around the corner from the Metro 12 line, Trinity station. There are some cafe's around the place to buy a cheap (relatively speaking) breakfast and it's in a good, quiet area. I like the decor and the rooms and bathrooms were adequate in size. On the negative side, I'd have to say that I was disappointed with thickness of the walls and floors. They cleaned our rooms every day but they didn't replace the towels which in the end isn't so bad but may bother others. Overall, I think I'd stay here again. I thought the price was reasonable at 96 euro per night.

This place allows you to actually move around instead of shimmying sideways to get from one side of the room to the other. The bathrooms and large and spacious too. There is a lift and though small, it does the trick. Unfortunately, and probably because it has grown so popular, it has gone up in price from when we paid around 79 euros with breakfast last year to this year where we most recently paid 96 euros with no breakfast. Still, for under 100 euro it is an amazing deal for Paris. You can walk to the Opera and the shopping streets easily and if there is anything out of your reach, the hotel is just around the corner from a metro stop, making gettting around very easy. This hotel will be the spice of your vacation.  
<Date>Feb 18, 2005

<Author>Ozzie_in_Ireland
<Content>Close to everything We stayed at the Hotel Langlois last week for 3 nights on a holiday visit.There were 7 in our party. My husband and I stayed in a double room, while my brother, his wife and their 3 children stayed in a suite which was very reasonably priced for so central a hotel. I had had a lot of trouble finding a budget hotel in central Paris that could accommodate my brother's family in one room, so after much searching on the web was delighted to see the reviews for the Hotel Langlois on this web site and took the chance of booking.We were all very happy with the hotel. It is perfectly situated for sight-seeing, and was within walking distance of the Louvre, Opera, Palais Royale, large department stores, the Roissy Bus, L'Open Tour Bus and Metro. There were a good number of restaurants (French and ethnic) nearby, though I would recommend trying to go further afield if you have a smaller party than ours, as we had difficulty finding any interesting or particularly French culinary treats close by apart from the cake shop next to the hotel and the creperie booth opposite the Trinity church. But the French restaurants nearby did offer good size portions of standard 'pub' fare and were helpful in regard to children's meals.The hotel itself was very clean, the breakfast buffet was fresh and there was plenty of it, and the hotel has obviously gone through a recent refurbishment. There are also many pleasing period features retained throughout the building. Our only complaint was that the rooms were very warm at night. But the weather was unseasonably mild during our stay, so the heating system may not have been able to adjust.

<Author>M0g
<Content>A Moveable Feast The well-travelled writer Ernest Hemingway once complimented Paris as being a moveable feast. Well, so is this hotel, for which we're indebted to this website and to those who've made such useful contributions to it. It's so helpful to have current opinions, even negative ones. Thus we weren't expecting a synthetically swish corporate hotel with robotic if multilingual staff. Just a small clean un-fussy well-run French establishment which offered value for money as well as some distinctively individual character. And that is exactly what we got. Room 15's bedroom and bathroom are both spacious and high-ceilinged and there's even an ante-room. Furniture and furnishings are suggestive of the building's history, but don't expect them to be pristine fresh - this is a deservedly popular hotel. There are no spectacular views from this first floor but you do overlook that section of the rue St Lazare, which is tucked away behind the Trinite Metro and is therefore relatively quiet and particularly so at night. The hotel's geographical convenience is well-documented on the website. And yes there are the usual suspects. The communal breakfast room on the ground floor is a bit of a squeeze. The buffet breakfast, though good value, is modest and mainly carbohydrate; that it's available for some four hours every morning allows for some flexibility about when you choose to eat but it does seem taxing for the one person who runs it. The central heating system works effectively if somewhat mysteriously so that when it was freezing or below outside we were always comfortable but the lack of air-conditioning would be an important consideration in summer. The management is, thankfully for us, very low-key; the reception staff handle things undemonstratively, pleasantly and competently; and with some geniality and tolerance if you try a few words of French. In our view the hotel entirely deserves its current high-rating. We very much hope it continues to maintain this standard and that that is monitored through subsequent reports on the Trip Advisor website. Enjoy the feast!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice Hotel for the Price Nice Hotel for the price, but can't believe it is a top 5 hotel in Paris. Staff were helpful but the maids did not speak English (we asked the desk clerk to translate and they were friendly). Our room had very squeeky floors and we could hear the people in the room next to us. This was a quaint hotel if your'e looking for the old Parisian feel. If you want a hot shower, shower at night. The patisserie near the hotel was great and it is 20 feet from the Metro stop and cash machine equally close. There are restaurants nearby. We liked Trinite Kebab, a small family-run diner type, the owner was extremely friendly and welcoming, and the prices were reasonable. The building was convereted into a hotel recently and is small (no workout room or formal dining room, although they do have a breakfast room). This was a cute hotel but not modern. Overall, a nice place to stay.

<Author>Dan504
<Content>Nice hotel, but not love at first sight. We read all of the reviews on this website before visiting this hotel a few weeks ago. We opted to upgrade our room to one with a larger bathroom based on recommendations of other users. This was our first trip to Paris, but our bathroom was very small and I was a bit surprised by this. Not worth the upgrade! Anyway, the view was amazing from the fifth floor (room 55) and the hotel certainly was charming. The location is great but we only discovered how close we were to incredible nightlife during the last day of our visit (our fault I guess). Less than two blocks away, across from the Trinity Church, is an amazing little bakery that has fantastic pressed sandwiches on baguettes. We picked up sandwiches before heading to Versailles and ate them on a bench just outside. The room itself was very dated, but completely clean. The television only really worked when it felt like it, but I guess you don't go to Paris to watch TV! It is a very noisy hotel, but we didn't really experience too many problems at night. The elevator is only big enough for two at the most, so we had to load all of our bags and walk up to the fifth floor, then unload. The staff is not very friendly, and I really did try to speak French with them (maybe it's my fault)! It sounds like I am complaining a lot here, but we really were satisfied with our stay. We had a fantastic vacation and I have no serious complaints. I think on our next trip to Paris, we'll try somewhere else. This one is a mixed bag -- if you want to be very comfortable, you may want to consider staying elsewhere.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A good alternative to big international hotels This is a very good alternative to a big (expensive) hotel. We stayed for four enjoyable nights in November 2004. You need to remember that it is a small boutique type hotel, but with that in mind and making allowances for the loss of facilities (no dining room etc), I can thoroughly recommend it. We had a good sized suite for 鈧?32 per night which is an absolute bargain. The breakfast was good and reasonable value at 鈧?. The staff were pleasant and helpful. The metro is nearby and you are handy for the Roissy Bus Stop to and from the airport. There are plenty of shops nearby and bars and restaurants are convenient.The drawbacks: the plumbing is antiquated and made quite a bit of noise, especially one night as we were trying to sleep. There is no air-conditioning so it might be hot in summer. The central heating was quite fierce as well and with the mild weather we were too hot most of the time. Nevertheless I think that this is a good choice for the money and although I do like luxury hotels I feel that this is an excellent compromise.Remember to try to speak a little French if you can, it will help!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good location and decent room We stayed at Hotel Langlois for 4 nights (18-22 Nov) and had room 62. The room was very clean and charming. Having said that we did experience not having enough hot water in the morning for showers and the room was not soundproof. We could hear all kinds of noises (i.e. elevator door opening/closing, footsteps in hallway, flushing of toilets, etc..) that prevented us from getting a good night sleep except on the last night when there were not alot of guests on the 6th floor.The receptionist recommeded a couple of great little restaurants in the area. Le Bistro Des Deux Theatres on 18 rue Blanche is an excellent restaurant that serves French food with a fixed menu of 32 Euro/person for a 3-course meal including coffee and a bottle of wine. Fuxi (sp?) is an Italian restaurant about 8-10 mins walk from the hotel and has very good Italian dishes. The price is very reasonable and the menu is la carte. We ordered off of the blackboard and was very pleased with our food.

The room wasnt that noisy in general. The first night i didnt sleep due to a noisy rattling window but overall i couldnt hear noise from other rooms. I agree with the last reviewer in that the metro is literally a 30 second walk away but then again there are so many stops on metro that other hotels are probably just as close so i wouldnt pick the hotel for this alone. I stayed in room 64 by the way. My overall advice would be dont bother with the 'superior room' save your ten euro night. Im beginning to think the large bathroom is only in suites? OK 50 night is not bad for paris but in some places that would include a ten euro's worth breakfast so is it really that good value?;o)

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastic Hotel We (two American photojournalists) stayed here for a four nights in mid-October while in Paris and loved the quaintness of the hotel. The rooms were decorated with antique furnishings and the bathroom (in room #11) was very charming. As a photographer, I found I just had to take several close still photographs of the charming bath faucet on the antique pedestal sink. That photograph will find its way onto one of the walls of my home outside Philadelphia and each time I pass it I will smile and remember my Paris experience. Room #15 was even better.I found that many on the staff were not completely comfortable speaking English, but who cares. Part of the charm of going to another country is trying to completely immerse yourself into the culture of the country and so, actually using my high school French was a good thing to do. I'd advise anyone visiting France to study a little French. That, and a smile, really works wonders in communicating anything from directions to menu items. And take a good dictionary.I'd stay at Hotel Langlois again and again and again. It allowed me to spend many more Euros on food, which is much more expensive. Terrific experience!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Breakfast, Convenient Location I stayed here with my husband for our honeymoon in September, 2004. The hotel is in an excellent location. The area feels safe and it's close to a subway station. We would wake up to amazing aroma of fresh baked goods each morning. Our room was generously big and it was facing a side street so it was very quiet. The breakfast at the hotel cost about 8 euros but my husband and I agree that it was one of the best we had in Paris. Fresh baked croissants, cheese, olives, cereals and all you can drink good coffee. The only thing to note is that their elevator and restrooms are very small. We would stay here again.

<Author>bopeltzman
<Content>Excellent value! If you want to be in the middle of the action, you may want to stay elsewhere (and pay a lot more); this hotel is a few blocks north-east of the l'Opera. I thought it was great; you get a real neighborhood feel and it was 1/2 block from the line 12 Metro. If you are going to be there for a week (like we were) take a small picture with you and get a Carte O'range at the station and you can ride anywhere in the city for about 20 Euros/week/person. We also had a large room with a very large bathroom. We skipped the breakfast and I went around the corner to the market for orange juice, yogurt (they must have 40+ different kinds) and apples and bananas for lunch snack, then to the patisserie (3 within a block) for fresh croisonts and a variety of quiches (which they will warm for you) and we ate in our room, overlooking the Paris roof tops, for $3 Euros./each. The small frig. will hold Coke, OJ, bottled water, wine, etc. The TV gets BBC and CNN. I agree that the owner is not overly friendly. She will only speak English if she has to but we only saw her one time (check in). The rest of the staff was friendly; we even stored a suitcase with them at no charge while we tooled off to the South of France for a week. There is no A/C (they give you a large floor fan); we were there in September with cool temperatures so we didn't need either. Would stay there again in a minute!

<Author>lass=
<Content>Great value hotel We stayed at the Hotel Langlois for a few nights in September on the recommendations in this forum. I was really pleased with our choice. Our room was 鈧?9 per night and was huge, with a massive bathroom. The hotel is so charming, and I loved the old-fashioned parisian style but if you prefer more modern surroundings it might not be to your taste. However, the rooms have modern electronic key-card locks, tv, mini-bar, hairdryer, phone etc so it has all the comforts you would expect. The rooms were quiet apart from the creaky floorboards which could be annoying, especially if you had kids running around on them. The breakfast is good value (鈧?.20) if you are happy with the continental style of tea, coffee, cornflakes, juice, croissants etc. There is no extra charge for having it brought to your room which is great  there is plenty of bread  croissants in one breakfast. One of the local cafes had a breakfast of tea/coffee, orange juice  croissant for 鈧?.50 so the hotel prices seem reasonable in comparison.The location is v. handy for the metro (~1 min walk) and for the shops :) Gallerie Lafeyette  Printemps are 5/10 mins away. We found the staff to be very polite  helpful with booking restaurants etc, and I would definitely go back to stay at this hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>very good but be aware Just got back from a 3 night stay after reading the reviews on this site. The hotel is very central and very clean but when booking it may be an idea to request a room on a higher floor or not facing the road - we were in room 14 which was very noisy and very hot ! Fortunately there was a large portable fan in the room which stayed on all night.Breakfast was disappointing - we weren't expecting a lot and that's what we got.If your idea of variety is the number of different jams then it's fine, but we thought 8.20euros was steep for cornflakes / mini pastries and bread rolls.If (like us) you're Easyjetting from Liverpool to Charles-de-Gaulle,save yourself some grief by catching the Roissybus which stops right outside Terminal 3 - it costs around 8 euros one way and stops at the Opera, which is only 10 minutes walk away from the hotel.Operates every 12 minutes and is very quick and easy - was faster than the RER which involves a train change at Gare Du Nord.At 89 euros for the double room and the central location this is a good choice - bear in mind that the most expensive room in the hotel is only 132 euros and it may be worth splashing out that little bit more !

<Content>Lived up to expectation My husband and I visited France in early August, 2 days in Paris, 2 days in Normandy and 2 more days in Paris. The location is great. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Hotel Langlois is a great value We stayed here for 10 days in late June/early July. We were in Room 21, which faced the courtyard, so had no view, but it was spacious, quiet, cool, and had lovely period furnishings. The staff was courteous, polite, and formal but never unpleasant. Breakfast was a good value, and there also is a lovely boulangerie several doors down from the hotel, which has wonderful croissants and eclairs. I stayed at a four-star hotel on a previous trip to Paris, but even though the Hotel Langlois lacks some amenities, such as a concierge, restaurant, and business center, it makes up for in charm and uniqueness. I definitely recommend this hotel.

<Author>Travel57
<Content>Mixed Feelings Visited in August 2004, lovely large room on 6th floor with view of Sacre Coeur. But not as good as I'd expected; smelly mould on shower curtain, which I reported to the staff. Only free standing fan to cool room - didn't enjoy listening to someone elses fan at night. Reception staff only spoke when absolutely necessary, I know Paris well and speak French but I think a welcoming smile and a greeting would make guests feel more welcome. The location is wonderful for the metro, but as a general location I'd not choose this hotel. I also stayed at the hotel louvre-forum on this visit and would prefer to stay there .

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Stay here! Good value,good location, good accomodation. An excellent hotel for a short break in Paris, with a good location close to the Opera and Gallerie Layfayette. The rooms are spacious with antique furniture and paintings. We had a top floor room with a rooftop view. Very nice! We could see the spires of Sacre-Coeur which was very romantic and atmospheric! The cafes nearby are very adequate for meals and much cheaper than those nearer the sights. The hotel staff were friendly but we found that only one spoke English well enough to help/ recommend restaurants etc. Would recommend this hotel and would definitely stay again.

<Author>Risky Aer
<Content>The Bees Knees. A really excellent small hotel in a very convenient location.Good matter of fact service with no obsequiousness or indifference and really athmospheric room (64,on top of the house with Sacre Coeur visible in the early morning sunshine above the surrounding rooftops).If anybody is used to the US style chain hotels then the Hotel de Langlois is NOT for you, but if its individualism at an affordable rate then it should be near the top of any consideration list.Downsides...... While breakfast is a good buffet spread, the FRESH fruit is in fact processed from a tin stuff.If U can live with that then away you go....I certainly would stay here again.
